API Primer

This page covers the universal interface of QAtlas.jl вҖ” the parts that apply regardless of which model or quantity you are working with. For model-specific documentation (Hamiltonian, parameters, stored quantities, verification cards) see the individual model pages under Models.

fetch вҖ” the primary entry point

QAtlas.fetch(model, quantity, bc; kwargs...) -> Number | NamedTuple
ArgumentTypeDescription
model<: AbstractModelThe physical model (e.g. TFIM(J=1.0, h=0.5))
quantity<: AbstractQuantityWhat to compute (e.g. Energy(:per_site))
bc<: BoundaryConditionSystem size / topology
kwargsvariesModel-specific parameters (e.g. ОІ, N)

The return type depends on the quantity:

  • Scalar quantities (Energy, MassGap, вҖҰ) вҶ’ Float64 or Rational
  • Multi-component quantities (CriticalExponents, AnyonStatistics, вҖҰ) вҶ’ NamedTuple
using QAtlas

# Scalar
E = QAtlas.fetch(TFIM(J=1.0, h=0.5), Energy(:per_site), OBC(16))

# NamedTuple
e = QAtlas.fetch(Universality(:Ising), CriticalExponents(); d=2)
e.ОІ    # 1//8
e.ОҪ    # 1//1

Boundary Conditions

OBC(N)        # open chain / slab of N sites
PBC(N)        # periodic ring of N sites
Infinite()    # thermodynamic limit (k-space / Bethe ansatz)

All three share the supertype BoundaryCondition. Not all models support all boundary conditions вҖ” see the Quantity Г— BC matrix on each model page.

Quantity types

Quantities are parameterised types whose type parameter encodes the variant of the quantity:

Energy(:total)       # total ground-state energy EвӮҖ
Energy(:per_site)    # EвӮҖ / N

FreeEnergy()         # F = -T ln Z (or -ОІвҒ»В№ ln Z)
ThermalEntropy()     # S = -вҲӮF/вҲӮT
SpecificHeat()       # C = -T вҲӮВІF/вҲӮTВІ

MassGap()            # many-body gap О” = EвӮҒ - EвӮҖ
CorrelationLength()  # Оҫ from exponential decay
CentralCharge()      # CFT central charge c

VonNeumannEntropy()  # S_vN = -tr(ПҒ ln ПҒ)
RenyiEntropy(Оұ)      # S_Оұ = (1-Оұ)вҒ»В№ ln tr(ПҒ^Оұ)

CriticalExponents()  # returns NamedTuple (ОІ, ОҪ, Оі, О·, Оҙ, Оұ, c)

All quantity types are subtypes of AbstractQuantity.

Model constructors

Every model is a Julia struct with keyword-argument fields for its physical parameters. Default values are always provided.

# Quantum spin models
TFIM(; J=1.0, h=1.0)
Heisenberg1D(; J=1.0)
XXZ1D(; J=1.0, О”=1.0)
Hubbard1D(; t=1.0, U=4.0)

# Classical lattice models
IsingSquare(; J=1.0)
IsingTriangular(; J=1.0)

# Universality classes
Universality(:Ising)        # equivalent to Universality{:Ising}()
MeanField()
MinimalModel(3, 4)          # M(p, p') minimal model
WZWSU2(k)                   # SU(2)_k WZW model

Checking what is implemented

QAtlas.implementation_status(TFIM())
# returns a Markdown table of all registered (quantity, bc) pairs

QAtlas.implementation_status_markdown(TFIM())
# same, as a String

Operator conventions

QAtlas standardises on the spin operator convention (S^Оұ with eigenvalues in {-S, вҖҰ, +S}) for all spin-observable return values. For fermionic and topological models, see the Conventions page.

See also

  • Models вҖ” per-model Hamiltonian, parameters, quantity matrix
  • Universality Classes вҖ” Universality{C} API
  • Conventions вҖ” operator normalisation rules
  • Verification вҖ” how correctness is ensured

Full API Index

QAtlas.REGISTRY вҖ” Constant
REGISTRY :: Vector{Implementation}

Module-level mutable vector populated at include-time by @register calls scattered across src/models/.../<Model>_registry.jl files. Public read API: implementation_status.

source
QAtlas._MAX_ED_SITES вҖ” Constant
_MAX_ED_SITES = 12

Hard cap on chain length for dense-ED helpers. 2^12 = 4096 вҶ’ 4096Г—4096 Hermitian eigendecomposition takes ~1 s on a laptop; 2^14 ~ 16384 is already several seconds and 64 GB+ of workspace, which is past the "cheap reference data" regime this helper targets.

source
QAtlas._MAX_ED_SITES_S1 вҖ” Constant
_MAX_ED_SITES_S1 = 8

Hard cap on chain length for spin-1 dense-ED helpers. 3вҒё = 6561 вҶ’ a 6561Г—6561 Hermitian eigendecomposition is ~1 s on a laptop; 3вҒ№ вүҲ 20 k already pushes 5 GB of workspace, past the "cheap reference" regime.

source
QAtlas.AKLT1D вҖ” Type
AKLT1D(; J::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Spin-1 bilinear-biquadratic chain at the AKLT point,

H = J ОЈбөў [ Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮҒ + (1/3) (Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮҒ)ВІ ],

with J > 0 antiferromagnetic. Same local Hilbert space as S1Heisenberg1D but with the biquadratic coefficient tuned to the special AKLT value 1/3 where the ground state is an exact Valence Bond Solid (VBS). The infinite-system observables exposed through fetch are closed-form (energy density, correlation length, string order parameter); the Haldane gap is the GarcГӯa-SaezвҖ“MurgвҖ“Verstraete (2013) DMRG numerical-exact value.

The constructor requires J > 0: the AKLT bond-projector decomposition H = 2J ОЈ PвӮӮ вҲ’ (2J/3) N_bonds and every analytic value registered in AKLT1D_registry.jl (GS energy density, correlation length, string order parameter, mass gap, ОІ=вҲһ thermodynamic limits) assumes the antiferromagnetic sign. Passing J вүӨ 0 would silently return sign-flipped or physically meaningless values, so the constructor throws ArgumentError at construction time instead.

source
QAtlas.AKLT2D вҖ” Type
AKLT2D(; J::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

2D honeycomb-lattice Affleck-Kennedy-Lieb-Tasaki (AKLT) spin-3/2 valence-bond-solid model. Frustration-free Hamiltonian whose unique gapped VBS ground state has exact energy density e0/N = 0 (J-independent); the 2D AKLT phase is the prototypical 2D symmetry-protected topological (SPT) state. See file header for full references.

source
QAtlas.AbstractModel вҖ” Type
const AbstractModel = AbstractQAtlasModel

Backward-compatible alias. Existing downstream code dispatches on ::AbstractModel; new code should use ::AbstractQAtlasModel directly or вҖ” preferably вҖ” a concrete model struct.

source
QAtlas.AbstractQAtlasModel вҖ” Type
AbstractQAtlasModel

Abstract parent type for every QAtlas model. Concrete subtypes carry their physics parameters as typed fields (e.g. struct TFIM <: AbstractQAtlasModel; J::Float64; h::Float64; end).

The older Model{S}(params::Dict) phantom-typed wrapper is still an AbstractQAtlasModel (via the deprecated alias below) but new models must use concrete structs.

source
QAtlas.AbstractQuantity вҖ” Type
AbstractQuantity

Abstract parent type for quantities. New code defines concrete structs (e.g. struct MagnetizationX <: AbstractQuantity end) so dispatch is static and naming is explicit (axis, entropy variant, вҖҰ). The older Quantity{S} phantom-type wrapper is retained for legacy symbol-based dispatch; see the Quantity(::Symbol) shim below.

source
QAtlas.AnyonStatistics вҖ” Type
AnyonStatistics() <: AbstractQuantity

Topological data of the anyon content of a 2D topologically ordered phase. The dispatched fetch method takes a type::Symbol kwarg selecting an anyon (or a mutual-braiding row) and returns a NamedTuple whose shape depends on the requested row вҖ” typically (label, statistics, self_phase, quantum_dim, fusion) for individual anyons, and (label, mutual_phase, anyons) for two-anyon braids.

For Abelian theories like the toric code's ZвӮӮ order all quantum dimensions are 1; for non-Abelian theories the schema is unchanged but quantum_dim becomes irrational and additional fields (e.g. F, R matrices) may be added by the implementing method.

Has no boundary-condition argument: anyon statistics are purely topological invariants.

source
QAtlas.BCFT вҖ” Type
BCFT() <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Boundary Conformal Field Theory with Cardy (1989) boundary states and Affleck-Ludwig (1991) g-functions.

Phase 1 ships only Ising-CFT Cardy boundary states; other CFTs (minimal models, free boson, WZW, вҖҰ) are tracked as Phase 2.

Quantities registered (Phase 1):

QuantityBCMethod
ResidualEntropyInfiniteanalytic log g for Ising Cardy states

The Cardy state is selected via the state keyword to fetch:

  • state=:fixed, :fixed_plus, :fixed_minus вҹ№ g = 1/вҲҡ2, log g = -log(2)/2 (physical fixed-spin boundaries, вүЎ (|1вҹ© Вұ |Оөвҹ©)/вҲҡ2)
  • state=:free вҹ№ g = 1, log g = 0 (physical free boundary, вүЎ the |Пғвҹ© Cardy state)
  • state=:sigma вҹ№ g = 1, log g = 0 (|Пғвҹ© Cardy state вҖ” alias of :free)
  • state=:identity, :vacuum вҹ№ g = 1/вҲҡ2, log g = -log(2)/2 (|1вҹ© Cardy state)
  • state=:epsilon, :energy вҹ№ g = 1/вҲҡ2, log g = -log(2)/2 (|Оөвҹ© Cardy state)

References

  • J. L. Cardy, Nucl. Phys. B 324, 581 (1989).
  • I. Affleck, A. W. W. Ludwig, Phys. Rev. Lett. 67, 161 (1991).
  • D. Friedan, A. Konechny, Phys. Rev. Lett. 93, 030402 (2004).
source
QAtlas.BoundaryCondition вҖ” Type
BoundaryCondition

Abstract parent type. The three concrete subtypes carry system-size information where applicable, so fetch can read it from the BC instead of kwargs.

  • Infinite вҖ” thermodynamic limit; no size.
  • PBC(N::Int) вҖ” periodic boundary conditions at finite N.
  • OBC(N::Int) вҖ” open boundary conditions at finite N.

For backward compatibility, the zero-argument constructors PBC() and OBC() exist and set N = 0, which signals "caller will pass N via kwargs" вҖ” legacy fetch methods still look at kwargs[:N]. New fetch methods read bc.N directly.

source
QAtlas.CasimirEnergyCorrection вҖ” Type
CasimirEnergyCorrection() <: AbstractQuantity

Universal 1/L finite-size correction to the ground-state energy of a 1+1D conformal field theory.

For a critical 1+1D system with central charge c and CFT velocity v on a system of size L:

  • Periodic boundary (PBC): $E_0(L) = L\,\varepsilon_\infty - \dfrac{\pi c v}{6 L} + O(L^{-2})$
  • Open boundary (OBC): $E_0(L) = L\,\varepsilon_\infty + \varepsilon_{\mathrm{surf}} - \dfrac{\pi c v}{24 L} + O(L^{-2})$

This quantity returns only the universal $1/L$ correction term ($-\pi c v/(6 L)$ at PBC, $-\pi c v/(24 L)$ at OBC), not the extensive $L \varepsilon_\infty$ piece nor the OBC surface term $\varepsilon_{\mathrm{surf}}$. The PBC-to-OBC ratio is exactly 4, independent of the universality class.

The CFT velocity v is model-dependent (e.g. $v = 2J$ for the TFIM at the critical point, $v = (\pi/2) J$ for the AFM Heisenberg chain, $v = v_F$ for the XXZ Luttinger liquid) and is supplied by the caller as a kwarg. The central charge c is read from the universality class via the same data the Universality{C} entry exposes for CriticalExponents.

References

  • J. Cardy, Nucl. Phys. B 270, 186 (1986).
  • H. W. J. BlГ¶te, J. L. Cardy, M. P. Nightingale, Phys. Rev. Lett. 56, 742 (1986).
  • I. Affleck, Phys. Rev. Lett. 56, 746 (1986).
Phase 2 (TODO)

The conformal tower of states вҖ“- primary scaling dimensions $(h, \bar h)$ and the $E_n - E_0 = (2\pi v/L)(h_n + \bar h_n)$ excitation pattern вҖ“- is tracked separately as future work (Phase 2 of issue #150) and will be exposed via a ConformalTower quantity once implemented.

source
QAtlas.CentralCharge вҖ” Type
CentralCharge() <: AbstractQuantity

Central charge c of the emergent CFT. For 1D critical systems extracted from the CalabreseвҖ“Cardy entanglement formula; universality pages return literature values.

source
QAtlas.ChargeGap вҖ” Type
ChargeGap() <: AbstractQuantity

Charge (Mott) gap of an electron system,

О”_c = EвӮҖ(N+1) + EвӮҖ(N-1) - 2 EвӮҖ(N),

i.e. the energy cost of adding a particle plus the cost of removing one, equivalent to the gap between the half-filled ground state and the lowest charged excitation. Strictly positive in a Mott insulator and exactly zero in a metal / superconductor.

Implemented analytically for Hubbard1D at half filling via the LiebвҖ“Wu (1968) closed-form integral.

source
QAtlas.ChernSimons3D вҖ” Type
ChernSimons3D(; N::Integer = 2, k::Integer = 1) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

3-D SU(N)k Chern-Simons TQFT (Witten 1989). N вүҘ 2 is the gauge- group rank-plus-one and `k вҲҲ в„Ө{>0}` is the (integer) Chern-Simons level.

Phase 1 exposed the boundary WZW central charge via the Sugawara construction. Phase 2 adds the closed-form SВі partition function Z(SВі; SU(N)_k) = S_{0,0} (Witten 1989 / Verlinde formula). Wilson-loop knot invariants and modular S / T matrices remain tracked for later phases.

Quantities registered:

QuantityBCMethod
CentralChargeInfiniteanalytic (Sugawara k(NВІ-1)/(k+N))
PartitionFunctionInfiniteanalytic (Witten Z(SВі) = modular S_{0,0})

References

  • E. Witten, Comm. Math. Phys. 121, 351 (1989).
  • V. G. Knizhnik, A. B. Zamolodchikov, Nucl. Phys. B 247, 83 (1984).
source
QAtlas.ChiralCondensate вҖ” Type
ChiralCondensate() <: AbstractQuantity

Vacuum expectation value вҹЁПҲМ„ПҲвҹ© of a fermion bilinear, signalling spontaneous (anomalous) chiral-symmetry breaking. The massless Schwinger model is the canonical 1+1-D example: even though the classical Lagrangian is chirally symmetric, the anomaly forces a non-zero condensate

вҹЁПҲМ„ПҲвҹ© = вҲ’ exp(Оі_E) В· e / (2ПҖ^{3/2}),    m_Оі = e/вҲҡПҖ.

(Schwinger 1962; Coleman-Jackiw-Susskind 1975.)

source
QAtlas.Cluster1D вҖ” Type
Cluster1D(; J::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

1D ZвӮӮГ—ZвӮӮ symmetry-protected topological cluster Hamiltonian H = -J ОЈ_i Пғ^z_{i-1} Пғ^x_i Пғ^z_{i+1}. Ground state is the cluster state (Briegel-Raussendorf 2001).

Quantities registered (Phase 1):

QuantityBCMethod
Energy (:per_site)Infiniteanalytic (stabiliser ground state)
MassGapInfiniteanalytic (single-stabiliser flip)

References

  • H. J. Briegel, R. Raussendorf, Phys. Rev. Lett. 86, 910 (2001).
  • D. V. Else, S. D. Bartlett, A. C. Doherty, New J. Phys. 14, 113016 (2012).
  • R. Verresen, R. Moessner, F. Pollmann, Phys. Rev. B 96, 165124 (2017).
source
QAtlas.Compass1D вҖ” Type
Compass1D(; J_x::Real = 1.0, J_y::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

1D alternating-bond compass chain

H = -J_x ОЈ_{i odd}  Пғ^x_i Пғ^x_{i+1}
    -J_y ОЈ_{i even} Пғ^y_i Пғ^y_{i+1},

with J_x, J_y > 0. Dual to a dimerised Kitaev / p-wave wire via JordanвҖ“Wigner; exactly solvable.

Phase 1 scope (this release)

Phase 1 exposes the closed-form bulk gap only:

  • MassGap at Infinite() вҶ’ О” = 2 |J_x вҲ’ J_y|.

The gap closes at the symmetric point J_x = J_y, which is a first-order quantum phase transition between the X-bond-dimerised and Y-bond-dimerised ground states (BrzezickiвҖ“DziarmagaвҖ“OleЕӣ 2007).

References

  • BrzezickiвҖ“DziarmagaвҖ“OleЕӣ, PRB 75, 134415 (2007).
  • KugelвҖ“Khomskii, Sov. Phys. Usp. 25, 231 (1982).
  • Kitaev, Annals of Physics 321, 2 (2006).
source
QAtlas.ConformalBootstrap вҖ” Type
ConformalBootstrap() <: AbstractQAtlasModel

The 3D Ising critical point with high-precision conformal-bootstrap scaling dimensions. Methodology: Kos-Poland-Simmons-Duffin 2014 (mixed-correlator bootstrap). Precise values: KPSD-Vichi 2016 "Precision Islands" (arXiv:1603.04436). Parameterless: the 3D Ising universality class is unique.

Phase 1 ships only the 3D Ising universality class; other bootstrap-pinned CFTs (O(N) vector models, stress-tensor and higher-spin multiplets, fermionic CFTs) are deferred to Phase 2.

Quantities registered (Phase 1):

QuantityBCMethod
ConformalWeightsInfinitebootstrap reference (KPSD 2016 islands)

Available kwargs for ConformalWeights:

  • field = :Пғ вҖ” lowest scalar primary, О”_Пғ = 0.51814894.
  • field = :Оө вҖ” lowest energy primary, О”_Оө = 1.41262528.

References

  • F. Kos, D. Poland, D. Simmons-Duffin, JHEP 06 (2014) 091 вҖ” methodology (mixed-correlator bootstrap).
  • F. Kos, D. Poland, D. Simmons-Duffin, A. Vichi, JHEP 08 (2016) 036; arXiv:1603.04436 вҖ” "Precision Islands", precise О”Пғ, О”Оө.
  • D. Simmons-Duffin, JHEP 03 (2017) 086 вҖ” lightcone-bootstrap cross-check.
  • M. Reehorst, S. Rychkov, D. Simmons-Duffin, B. Sirois, N. Su, B. van Rees, SciPost Phys. 11 (2021) 072.
source
QAtlas.ConformalWeights вҖ” Type
ConformalWeights() <: AbstractQuantity

Primary scaling dimension h of a 2D rational CFT. For Virasoro MinimalModel this is the Kac-table entry h_{r,s}; for WZWSU2 it is the SU(2)-spin label h_j = j(j+1)/(k+2).

Concrete model fetch methods take additional keyword arguments identifying the primary (r, s for MinimalModel; j for WZWSU2) and return an exact Rational{Int}.

source
QAtlas.CorrelationLength вҖ” Type
CorrelationLength() <: AbstractQuantity

Two-point correlation length Оҫ controlling the exponential decay of connected equal-time correlators in a gapped phase,

вҹЁПғ_Оұ(0) Пғ_Оұ(r)вҹ©_c ~ e^{-r/Оҫ}    (r вҶ’ вҲһ).

For a critical system Оҫ = вҲһ; implementations return Inf in that case. At T = 0 and 1D free-fermion models like TFIM, Оҫ is set by the inverse mass gap (Оҫ = 1/(2|h - J|)).

source
QAtlas.CriticalExponents вҖ” Type
CriticalExponents() <: AbstractQuantity

Standard set of equilibrium critical exponents {Оұ, ОІ, Оі, Оҙ, ОҪ, О·} of a universality class. Returns a NamedTuple.

For exact values: fields are Rational{Int}. For numerical estimates: fields are Float64 with corresponding _err fields (e.g., ОІ_err) giving the uncertainty.

source
QAtlas.CriticalTemperature вҖ” Type
CriticalTemperature() <: AbstractQuantity

Exact critical temperature of a classical model.

source
QAtlas.CurieWeissIsing вҖ” Type
CurieWeissIsing(; J::Real = 1.0, h::Real = 0.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Classical Ising model on the complete graph (mean field) with saddle-point Hamiltonian

H = -(J/N) ОЈ_{i<j} Пғ_i Пғ_j  -  h ОЈ_i Пғ_i.

The 1/N normalisation makes the energy extensive and the thermodynamic limit well-defined. At h = 0 and J > 0 the model has zero-field critical temperature T_c = J and mean-field critical exponents (ОІ, Оі, Оҙ, ОҪ) = (1/2, 1, 3, 1/2) exposed by Universality(:MeanField).

For h вү  0 there is no sharp transition; the equilibrium magnetisation m*(ОІ, J, h) is the unique stable root of the self-consistency equation m = tanh(ОІ(Jm + h)) (same sign as h).

Quantities registered:

QuantityBCNotes
CriticalTemperatureInfiniteJ (h = 0 reference)
SpontaneousMagnetizationInfiniteh вҶ’ 0вҒә limit (independent of model.h)
CriticalExponentsInfiniteMeanField universality
Energy{:per_site}Infinite-JmВІ/2 - hm
FreeEnergyInfiniteJmВІ/2 - ОІвҒ»В№ log[2 cosh(ОІ(Jm+h))]
ThermalEntropyInfinitelog[2cosh(ОІ(Jm+h))] - ОІ(Jm+h)m
SpecificHeatInfiniteОІВІ(Jm+h)ВІ(1-mВІ)/(1-ОІJ(1-mВІ))
SusceptibilityZZInfiniteОІ(1-mВІ)/(1-ОІJ(1-mВІ))

References

  • L. D. Landau, E. M. Lifshitz, Statistical Physics В§149.
source
QAtlas.DMIHeisenberg1D вҖ” Type
DMIHeisenberg1D(; J::Real = 1.0, D::Real = 0.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Spin-ВҪ Heisenberg chain with Dzyaloshinskii-Moriya interaction along бә‘:

H = J ОЈ_i Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮҒ + D ОЈ_i (SбөўЛЈ SбөўвӮҠвӮҒКё вҲ’ SбөўКё SбөўвӮҠвӮҒЛЈ),    J > 0,  D вҲҲ в„қ.

Phase 1 implements only the closed-form D = 0 point (pure Heisenberg), delegating to Heisenberg1D. Generic D вү  0 introduces a spiral ground state via a gauge mapping to a twisted XXZ chain (Affleck- Oshikawa 1999); closed-form energy is technically Bethe-ansatz-tractable on the gauged model but is deferred to Phase 2, raising DomainError from fetch(..., Energy{:per_site}(), Infinite()).

The default constructor DMIHeisenberg1D() lands on J = 1, D = 0 вҖ” the Bethe-HulthГ©n point, the only Phase-1 closed-form case.

Fields

  • J::Float64 вҖ” Heisenberg exchange (J > 0 antiferromagnetic).
  • D::Float64 вҖ” DM coupling along бә‘ (any real).

References

  • H. Bethe, Z. Physik 71, 205 (1931).
  • L. HulthГ©n, Ark. Mat. Astron. Fys. 26A, No. 11 (1938).
  • I. E. Dzyaloshinskii, J. Phys. Chem. Solids 4, 241 (1958).
  • T. Moriya, Phys. Rev. 120, 91 (1960).
  • I. Affleck, M. Oshikawa, Phys. Rev. B 60, 1038 (1999).
source
QAtlas.E8 вҖ” Type
E8() <: AbstractQAtlasModel

The E8 integrable field theory вҖ” the low-energy continuum theory of the 2D Ising model perturbed by a small longitudinal magnetic field at T = T_c (Zamolodchikov 1989). The only physics parameter is the underlying magnetic field perturbation strength, but QAtlas currently only exposes the universal mass-ratio spectrum, so this struct carries no fields.

source
QAtlas.E8Spectrum вҖ” Type
E8Spectrum() <: AbstractQuantity

Zamolodchikov E8 mass spectrum (8 stable particles). Concrete implementation lives in src/universalities/E8.jl; the type is defined here so src/core/alias.jl can reference it without circular loads.

source
QAtlas.EdgeModeEnergy вҖ” Type
EdgeModeEnergy() <: AbstractQuantity

Energy of the lowest-lying boundary mode on an open chain. In a topological 1D superconductor (Kitaev 2001) the OBC chain hosts two Majorana zero modes at the chain ends; their hybridization energy decays exponentially with chain length,

\[E_\text{edge}(N) \sim e^{-N/\xi},\]

where Оҫ is the bulk correlation length. In the trivial phase the OBC lowest single-particle excitation is set by the bulk gap.

EdgeModeEnergy is the smallest positive BdG eigenvalue of the OBC chain вҖ” the same quantity as MassGap at OBC, exposed under a name that makes the boundary-mode interpretation explicit at the call site.

Currently used by Kitaev1D.

source
QAtlas.Energy вҖ” Type
Energy{G}() <: AbstractQuantity
Energy()                 # G = :natural вҖ” model-and-BC-natural granularity
Energy(:total)           # explicit вҹЁHвҹ©
Energy(:per_site)        # explicit вҹЁHвҹ© / N

Ground-state / thermal energy expectation. The type parameter G makes the granularity (total vs per-site) a dispatch axis instead of a hidden docstring contract.

Energy() resolves to the model's native granularity via the native_energy_granularity trait вҖ” keeping every existing fetch(model, Energy(), bc; ...) call site working unchanged. Use the explicit constructors when the caller needs a specific granularity (e.g. the thermodynamic-identity harness comparing f + TВ·s against per-site Оө).

The non-native granularity is provided automatically by a generic conversion fallback for 1D BCs (OBC / PBC) that uses _bc_size. Models on lattices whose size is not captured by bc.N (e.g. 2D Kitaev with Lx, Ly kwargs) currently support only their declared native granularity.

ExtendedHubbard1D(; t::Real = 1.0, U::Real = 4.0, V::Real = 0.0)
    <: AbstractQAtlasModel

1D t-U-V Hubbard chain (nearest-neighbour-density extension of the standard Hubbard model):

H = -t ОЈ_{i, Пғ} (cвҖ _{i,Пғ} c_{i+1,Пғ} + h.c.)
    + U ОЈ_i n_{i,вҶ‘} n_{i,вҶ“}
    + V ОЈ_i n_i n_{i+1}.

Convention: t > 0 hopping, U on-site, V nearest-neighbour density-density.

Phase 1 scope (this release)

Phase 1 exposes only the V = 0 limit, at which the model reduces to the standard 1D Hubbard chain. The ChargeGap at Infinite() is delegated to Hubbard1D at half filling (Ој = U/2), i.e. the LiebвҖ“Wu (1968) integral

О”_c = (16 tВІ / U) вҲ«_1^вҲһ dПү  вҲҡ(ПүВІ - 1) / sinh(2ПҖ t Пү / U).

Any V вү  0 raises DomainError. The V вү  0 phase diagram (CDW / SDW / BOW / phase separation, Voit 1995; Nakamura 2000) is deferred to Phase 2.

References

  • Lieb, Wu, Phys. Rev. Lett. 20, 1445 (1968).
  • Voit, Rep. Prog. Phys. 58, 977 (1995).
  • Nakamura, Phys. Rev. B 61, 16377 (2000).

QAtlas.FibonacciAnyons вҖ” Type
FibonacciAnyons <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Non-Abelian Fibonacci anyon model.

The anyon spectrum has two charges {1, П„} with the fusion rule

П„ Г— П„ = 1 + П„

and quantum dimensions

d_1 = 1,   d_П„ = ПҶ = (1 + вҲҡ5)/2  (golden ratio).

Total quantum dimension

рқ’ҹ = вҲҡ(d_1ВІ + d_П„ВІ) = вҲҡ(1 + ПҶВІ) = вҲҡ(ПҶ + 2)

(using ПҶВІ = ПҶ + 1).

Fibonacci anyons are universal for topological quantum computation (Freedman-Kitaev-Larsen-Wang 2003) and arise as edge excitations of the Read-Rezayi Z_3 parafermion state (Read-Rezayi 1999).

This model has no continuous parameters вҖ” the spectrum and quantum dimensions are fixed by the fusion rules.

References

  • M. Freedman, A. Kitaev, M. Larsen, Z. Wang, Bull. Amer. Math. Soc. 40, 31 (2003).
  • N. Read, E. Rezayi, Phys. Rev. B 59, 8084 (1999).
  • A. Kitaev, J. Preskill, Phys. Rev. Lett. 96, 110404 (2006).
  • M. Levin, X.-G. Wen, Phys. Rev. Lett. 96, 110405 (2006).

QAtlas.GGEValue вҖ” Type
GGEValue{Q<:AbstractQuantity}(inner) <: AbstractQuantity

Wrapper quantity carrying an underlying observable inner::Q whose generalised Gibbs ensemble (GGE) stationary value is to be computed вҖ” i.e. the t вҶ’ вҲһ long-time average that an integrable (free-fermion) quench reaches.

For an integrable system the ordinary (canonical) Gibbs ensemble does not describe the long-time relaxed state: every mode-occupation n_k = вҹЁc_kвҖ  c_kвҹ© is a separate conserved quantity, so the diagonal ensemble is a generalised Gibbs ensemble fixed by the full distribution {n_k}. See Rigol et al. PRL 98, 050405 (2007) for the foundational argument and Calabrese, Essler, Fagotti J. Stat. Mech. (2012) P07016 / P07022 for the TFIM-specific closed-form expressions.

fetch(model_f, ::GGEValue{Q}, bc; initial::ModelType, kwargs...) returns the GGE expectation of the Q observable in the post-quench Hamiltonian model_f, with the conserved mode occupations frozen by the initial-state (initial) Bogoliubov rotation.

Construction

GGEValue(Energy())                  # вҹЁH_fвҹ© stationary value
GGEValue(MagnetizationX())          # вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ© stationary value

Fetch signature (TFIM)

fetch(TFIM(h = h_f), GGEValue(Energy()), Infinite();
      initial = TFIM(h = h_0)) -> Float64

A no-quench limit h_0 = h_f reduces to the static ground-state value of the inner observable.

Phase 1 registered the UV free-fermion central charge at g = 0. Phase 2 (#247) adds the large-N dynamical mass m_F = Оӣ exp(-ПҖ/(N gВІ)) via MassGap. Andrei-Lowenstein exact S-matrix and the chiral condensate remain tracked as Phase 3.

Quantities registered:

QuantityBCMethod
CentralChargeInfiniteanalytic (c = N at the free point)
MassGapInfiniteanalytic (Оӣ exp(-ПҖ/(N gВІ)), large-N)

References

  • D. J. Gross, A. Neveu, Phys. Rev. D 10, 3235 (1974).
  • N. Andrei, J. H. Lowenstein, Phys. Rev. Lett. 43, 1698 (1979).

QAtlas.Hubbard1D вҖ” Type
Hubbard1D(; t::Real = 1.0, U::Real = 4.0, Ој::Real = 2.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

1D Hubbard model

H = -t ОЈ_{i, Пғ} (cвҖ _{i,Пғ} c_{i+1,Пғ} + h.c.)
    + U ОЈ_i n_{i,вҶ‘} n_{i,вҶ“}
    - Ој ОЈ_i n_i

Convention: t > 0 hopping, U > 0 on-site repulsion. Half filling corresponds to Ој = U/2 (particle-hole-symmetric point).

Phase 1 scope (this release)

Phase 1 implements the LiebвҖ“Wu (1968) closed-form integrals at half filling only (Ој = U/2). The supported Infinite() quantities are

  • GroundStateEnergyDensity вҖ” EвӮҖ/N via the LiebвҖ“Wu integral,
  • ChargeGap вҖ” Mott gap О”_c via the LiebвҖ“Wu second integral,
  • SpinGap вҖ” 0 exactly (rigorous gapless-spinon result).

Off half filling raises a DomainError вҖ” the general-filling (coupled-integral-equation) and finite-temperature (QTM) surfaces are deferred to Phase 2.

IsingChain1D(; J::Real = 1.0, h::Real = 0.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Classical 1-D Ising chain with nearest-neighbour exchange J and uniform longitudinal field h:

О»_Вұ = e^{ОІ J} cosh(ОІ h) Вұ вҲҡ( e^{2 ОІ J} sinhВІ(ОІ h) + e^{-2 ОІ J} ).

Classical 2D Ising model on a square lattice with periodic boundary conditions (PBC) in both directions.

Hamiltonian: H = -J ОЈ_{вҹЁi,jвҹ©} Пғбөў Пғвұј, Пғбөў вҲҲ {-1, +1}.

Physics parameters are carried as typed struct fields:

QAtlas.IsingTriangular вҖ” Type
IsingTriangular(; J::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Classical 2D Ising model on the triangular lattice with the Wannier 1950 sign convention

H = +J ОЈ_{вҹЁi,jвҹ©} Пғ_i Пғ_j,   Пғ_i вҲҲ {-1, +1}.

The coupling sign determines the physics:

  • J > 0 вҖ” antiferromagnetic, frustrated. The triangular plaquette cannot satisfy all three antiferromagnetic bonds simultaneously, so the ground-state manifold is macroscopically degenerate and there is no long-range order at any $T > 0$ (Wannier 1950).
  • J < 0 вҖ” ferromagnetic. The lattice supports a standard order-disorder transition at $T_c = 4|J| / \ln 3$ (Houtappel 1950).
  • J = 0 вҖ” non-interacting; degenerate value preserved for symmetry.

Quantities currently registered for this model:

QuantityBCMethod
CriticalTemperatureInfiniteanalytic
ResidualEntropyInfiniteanalytic (QuadGK)
Sign convention differs from `IsingSquare`

IsingTriangular uses the Wannier 1950 convention H = +J ОЈ ПғПғ, so J > 0 means antiferromagnetic (frustrated). By contrast, IsingSquare uses the modern H = -J ОЈ ПғПғ convention where J > 0 means ferromagnetic. Passing the same numerical value of J to the two models therefore selects opposite physics. To keep the user-facing critical-temperature comparison meaningful: IsingSquare(J=1.0) (FM) вҶ” IsingTriangular(J=-1.0) (FM).

See also: IsingSquare for the square-lattice (non-frustrated) counterpart with the Onsager / Yang closed forms.

source
QAtlas.J1J2Heisenberg1D вҖ” Type
J1J2Heisenberg1D(; J1::Real = 1.0, J2::Real = 0.5) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Spin-ВҪ JвӮҒ-JвӮӮ Heisenberg chain:

H = JвӮҒ ОЈ_i Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮҒ + JвӮӮ ОЈ_i Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮӮ,    JвӮҒ > 0,  JвӮӮ вүҘ 0.

Define the frustration ratio j = JвӮӮ / JвӮҒ. Phase 1 implements only the two closed-form points:

  • j = 0 вҶ’ Bethe-HulthГ©n E/N = JвӮҒ (1/4 вҲ’ ln 2),
  • j = 1/2 вҶ’ Majumdar-Ghosh E/N = вҲ’3 JвӮҒ / 8.

Generic j (0 < j < вҲһ, j вҲү {0, 1/2}) requires DMRG; deferred to Phase 2, raises DomainError from fetch(..., Energy{:per_site}(), Infinite()).

The default constructor J1J2Heisenberg1D() lands on JвӮҒ = 1, JвӮӮ = 1/2 вҖ” the Majumdar-Ghosh point, the most physically interesting closed-form case.

Fields

  • J1::Float64 вҖ” nearest-neighbour antiferromagnetic exchange (JвӮҒ > 0).
  • J2::Float64 вҖ” next-nearest-neighbour exchange (JвӮӮ вүҘ 0).

References

  • H. Bethe, Z. Physik 71, 205 (1931).
  • L. HulthГ©n, Ark. Mat. Astron. Fys. 26A, No. 11 (1938).
  • C. K. Majumdar, D. K. Ghosh, J. Math. Phys. 10, 1388 (1969).
  • S. R. White, I. Affleck, Phys. Rev. B 54, 9862 (1996).

QAtlas.Kitaev1D вҖ” Type
Kitaev1D(; Ој = 0.0, t = 1.0, О” = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Kitaev (2001) one-dimensional p-wave superconducting wire,

\[H = -\mu \sum_i c_i^{\dagger} c_i - t \sum_i (c_i^{\dagger} c_{i+1} + \text{h.c.}) + \Delta \sum_i (c_i c_{i+1} + \text{h.c.}).\]

Ој is the chemical potential, t the hopping, О” the p-wave pairing. |Ој| < 2|t| is the topological phase (Majorana edge modes); |Ој| > 2|t| is the trivial phase; |Ој| = 2|t| is the gapless critical line.

This is the 1D Majorana wire and is distinct from the 2D KitaevHoneycomb spin model.

The TFIM is a special case (Ој = -2h, t = J, О” = J); the BdG spectrum of Kitaev1D(Ој=-2h, t=J, О”=J) agrees exactly with that of TFIM(J=J, h=h) at OBC.

QAtlas.LogarithmicCFT вҖ” Type
LogarithmicCFT <: AbstractQAtlasModel

The c = 0 logarithmic conformal field theory describing the universality class of self-avoiding polymers (Saleur 1992), critical percolation (Cardy 2001), and dilute / dense polymer phases.

The theory is logarithmic because the dilatation operator L_0 admits indecomposable (non-diagonalisable) Jordan blocks вҖ” pairs of primary fields share scaling dimensions but mix under conformal transformations, producing logarithms in correlation functions. The total central charge identically vanishes, yet the theory is non-trivial (Pearce-Rasmussen-Zuber 2006; Vasseur-Jacobsen-Saleur 2011).

Phase 1 exposes only CentralCharge = 0. Logarithmic-operator structure, indecomposable representations, and specific ОІ-coupling parametrisations are deferred to Phase 2.

source

J > 0 (ferromagnetic), h > 0 (transverse field), Оұ > 0 (decay exponent). The default Оұ = Inf sits at the nearest-neighbour TFIM point, for which the gap is known in closed form.

QAtlas.LongRangeXY1D вҖ” Type
LongRangeXY1D(; J::Real = 1.0, h::Real = 0.0, Оұ::Real = Inf)
    <: AbstractQAtlasModel

1D XY chain with power-law-decaying interactions in a transverse field:

H = -J ОЈ_{i<j} (ПғбөўЛЈ ПғвұјЛЈ + ПғбөўКё ПғвұјКё) / |i-j|^Оұ  -  h ОЈбөў Пғбөўб¶».

Constraints: J > 0, Оұ > 0, h вҲҲ в„қ.

Quantities registered (Phase 1):

QuantityBCMethod
MassGapInfiniteanalytic, Оұ = Inf NN XX limit (LSM)

Phase 1 exposes only the Оұ = Inf nearest-neighbour XX-in-transverse-field limit, whose mass gap is the closed form О” = 2В·max(0, |h| - 2J) (Lieb-Schultz-Mattis 1961, isotropic XX limit of the XY chain; Pfeuty 1970 for the TFIM-context derivation). Finite Оұ raises DomainError pending the Phase 2 DMRG follow-up (Maghrebi-Gong-Gorshkov 2017 for the XY chain power-law family).

References

  • E. Lieb, T. Schultz, D. Mattis, Annals Phys. 16, 407 (1961).
  • P. Pfeuty, Annals Phys. 57, 79 (1970).

QAtlas.LoschmidtEcho вҖ” Type
LoschmidtEcho{M}() <: AbstractQuantity
LoschmidtEcho(:amplitude)
LoschmidtEcho(:rate)
LoschmidtRateFunction()        # alias for LoschmidtEcho{:rate}

Loschmidt-echo family for sudden-quench dynamics. After preparing |ПҲ_0вҹ© as the ground state of an "initial" model H_0 and quenching to the "final" model H_f (passed as the first positional argument to fetch), the Loschmidt amplitude is

G(t) = вҹЁПҲ_0 | e^{-i H_f t} | ПҲ_0вҹ©,

with the Loschmidt echo L(t) = |G(t)|ВІ вҲҲ [0, 1] and the rate function

О»(t) = -log L(t) / N         (finite N)
О»(t) = -lim_{NвҶ’вҲһ} log L(t)/N (thermodynamic limit / Infinite)

Non-analytic cusps in О»(t) are dynamical quantum phase transitions (DQPT). See Heyl, Polkovnikov, Kehrein, PRL 110, 135704 (2013) and the review Heyl, Rep. Prog. Phys. 81, 054001 (2018).

The mode M::Symbol вҲҲ (:amplitude, :rate) is a phantom type parameter so that :amplitude (returns L(t)) and :rate (returns О»(t)) dispatch separately. The convenience alias LoschmidtRateFunction is the only flavour defined for Infinite, since the :amplitude itself is identically zero in the thermodynamic limit (extensive cumulants).

The pre-quench Hamiltonian is passed via the initial keyword on fetch, e.g.

fetch(TFIM(J=1.0, h=0.5), LoschmidtRateFunction(), Infinite();
      initial=TFIM(J=1.0, h=2.0), t=1.0)
source
QAtlas.LoschmidtRateFunction вҖ” Type
const LoschmidtRateFunction = LoschmidtEcho{:rate}

Convenience alias for the rate-function flavour О»(t) = -log L(t)/N. See LoschmidtEcho.

QAtlas.LuttingerVelocity вҖ” Type
LuttingerVelocity() <: AbstractQuantity

Luttinger-liquid / bosonisation velocity u (a.k.a. v_{LL}) of the low-energy linear-dispersion mode in a 1D critical interacting system. Used by models like XXZ1D in the Luttinger regime |О”| < 1, the Heisenberg chain at the SU(2) point, and any other bosonised 1D critical theory.

For a free-fermion model this coincides with FermiVelocity; for interacting systems u includes the Luttinger renormalisation.

QAtlas.MagnetizationXLocal вҖ” Type
MagnetizationXLocal{M}() <: AbstractQuantity
MagnetizationXLocal()                       # M = :equilibrium (default)
MagnetizationXLocal(:equilibrium)           # explicit equilibrium вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©_ОІ
MagnetizationXLocal(:quench)                # post-quench вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©(t)

Site-resolved вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ© quantity. The mode parameter M::Symbol is a phantom type that splits the dispatch into:

  • :equilibrium вҖ” site-resolved thermal expectation [вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©_ОІ for i = 1:N] (Vector{Float64}). This is the original meaning; the no-argument constructor MagnetizationXLocal() keeps back-compatibility by routing here.

  • :quench вҖ” time-evolved local transverse magnetisation вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©(t) = вҹЁПҲ_0|e^{iH_f t} ПғЛЈ_i e^{-iH_f t}|ПҲ_0вҹ© after a sudden quench from the ground state of an initial::AbstractQAtlasModel (H_0) to the post-quench Hamiltonian (the model argument to fetch). Returns a single Float64 for one (i, t) pair.

See docs/src/calc/tfim-sigma-x-quench.md for the closed-form derivation in the TFIM (CalabreseвҖ“EsslerвҖ“Fagotti, J. Stat. Mech. P07016 (2012); BarouchвҖ“McCoyвҖ“Dresden, PRA 2 (1970)).

QAtlas.MajumdarGhosh вҖ” Type
MajumdarGhosh(; J::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Spin-ВҪ MajumdarвҖ“Ghosh chain вҖ” the JвӮҒвҖ“JвӮӮ Heisenberg chain locked to the special ratio JвӮӮ/JвӮҒ = 1/2:

H = J ОЈ_i Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮҒ + (J/2) ОЈ_i Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮӮ,   S = 1/2.

At this point the ground state is exactly the product of nearest- neighbour singlets (two-fold degenerate), with size-independent ground- state energy density EвӮҖ/N = вҲ’3J/8. An analytical lower bound on the gap О” вүҲ 0.234 J (default) is from White-Affleck DMRG (1996; reproduced by Eggert 1996); a separately-labelled trimer-sector lower bound О”_trimer вүҘ J/4 is exposed via method=:trimer_bound (Shastry- Sutherland 1981). Note: the SS bound exceeds the actual DMRG gap, so it is best read as a sector-specific bound (see MassGap docstring).

Fields

  • J::Float64 вҖ” antiferromagnetic exchange coupling (J > 0). The next-nearest-neighbour coupling is locked to J/2 by the model definition.

References

  • C. K. Majumdar, D. K. Ghosh, J. Math. Phys. 10, 1388 (1969).
  • B. S. Shastry, B. Sutherland, J. Phys. C 14, L765 (1981).
  • S. R. White, I. Affleck, Phys. Rev. B 54, 9862 (1996).

QAtlas.MinimalModel вҖ” Type
MinimalModel(p::Int, p_prime::Int) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Virasoro minimal model M(p, pprime). p and `pprimemust be coprime integers withp > p_prime вүҘ 2. Construction validates those conditions and throwsDomainError` otherwise.

Special cases (cross-check):

Model(p, p_prime)c
YangвҖ“Lee (non-unitary)(5, 2)-22/5
Ising(4, 3)1/2
Tricritical Ising(5, 4)7/10
3-state Potts (chiral)(6, 5)4/5

The Ising special case MinimalModel(4, 3) reproduces the central charge stored in Universality(:Ising)'s CriticalExponents table (c = 1//2).

Use fetch with CentralCharge or ConformalWeights:

fetch(MinimalModel(4, 3), CentralCharge())                  # 1//2
fetch(MinimalModel(4, 3), ConformalWeights(); r=1, s=2)     # 1//16

See also: WZWSU2, Universality, CentralCharge, ConformalWeights, PrimaryFields.

QAtlas.MixedFieldIsing1D вҖ” Type
MixedFieldIsing1D(; J = 1.0, h_x = 1.0, h_z = 0.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

The 1D mixed-field Ising chain

H = -J ОЈ_i Пғб¶»_i Пғб¶»_{i+1} - h_x ОЈ_i ПғЛЈ_i - h_z ОЈ_i Пғб¶»_i,    J > 0.

The default h_z = 0.0 sits on the Phase-1 closed-form point where the model coincides with the standard TFIM (О”_вҲһ = 2|h_x вҲ’ J|, gap closing at the quantum critical point h_x = J).

At h_z вү  0 the model is non-integrable вҖ” fetch methods will throw DomainError in Phase 1 and route to numerical solvers in Phase 2.

QAtlas.RenyiEntropy вҖ” Type

RГ©nyi entropy of order Оұ, S_Оұ = (1 вҲ’ Оұ)вҒ»В№ log Tr ПҒ_A^Оұ.

  • Оұ = 1 recovers VonNeumannEntropy (implementations may dispatch accordingly).
  • Оұ = 2 is the second RГ©nyi entropy, frequently measured experimentally.
  • Оұ > 0, Оұ вү  1 are the supported generic cases.

The inner constructor rejects Оұ вүӨ 0 and Оұ = 1 (use VonNeumannEntropy() explicitly) вҖ” this is intentional, to force the call site to be explicit about which entropy it wants.

source
QAtlas.ResidualEntropy вҖ” Type
ResidualEntropy() <: AbstractQuantity

Zero-temperature configurational (residual) entropy density. Real- valued, non-negative; non-zero in the presence of macroscopic ground-state degeneracy (e.g. ice rule, frustrated Ising AFM, Pauling-1935-style models). Distinct from ThermalEntropy: ThermalEntropy is a finite-temperature thermodynamic quantity, while ResidualEntropy is the lim_{T -> 0} S(T) / N residual term. Zero-temperature ground-state entropy per site,

S_residual / (N k_B) = lim_{T вҶ’ 0вҒә} S(T) / N,

i.e. the entropy density of the (possibly degenerate) ground-state manifold. Non-zero for frustrated classical models with extensive ground-state degeneracy вҖ” e.g. the antiferromagnetic Ising model on the triangular lattice (Wannier 1950, вүҲ 0.3230659669) and on the kagome lattice (Houtappel 1950). Defined as a separate quantity from ThermalEntropy to keep the zero-temperature limit explicit at the dispatch level (avoiding ОІ вҶ’ вҲһ extrapolations of a finite-T fetch).

source
QAtlas.S1AnisotropicD1D вҖ” Type

Any D вү  0 raises DomainError вҖ” finite-D crosses Gaussian (large-D) and Ising (NГ©el) transitions whose closed forms are unknown and are deferred to the DMRG-based Phase 2 (Chen-Roncaglia 2008; Tzeng-Yang-Hsu 2017).

QAtlas.SYK вҖ” Type
SYK(; q::Integer = 4) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Sachdev-Ye-Kitaev model: N Majorana fermions with all-to-all random q-body coupling. The defining structural parameter for the universal large-N IR is q (which must be even вҖ” Majorana antisymmetry вҖ” and вүҘ 2). The fermion number N and the coupling scale J set the UV / finite-N data but do not enter the leading large-N IR conformal dimension exposed here.

Default q = 4 is the most-studied case: 4-body Majorana coupling, exactly soluble Schwarzian-dressed two-point function, and a maximal Lyapunov exponent saturating the Maldacena- Shenker-Stanford bound.

Quantities registered (Phase 1):

QuantityBCMethod
ConformalWeightsInfiniteanalytic large-N IR (О”_ПҲ = 1/q)

Phase 2 will add composite-operator dimensions (bilinear tower), the Schwarzian zero-T entropy, maximal Lyapunov saturation, and the JT-gravity bulk dual.

References

  • S. Sachdev, J. Ye, Phys. Rev. Lett. 70, 3339 (1993).

  • J. Maldacena, D. Stanford, Phys. Rev. D 94, 106002 (2016).

ShastrySutherland(; J::Real = 0.0, Jp::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

  1. the ground state is the exact product of nearest-neighbour

singlets on the diagonal (Jp) bonds вҖ” the 2-D analog of the MajumdarвҖ“Ghosh dimer state.

QuantityBCMethod
Energy (:per_site)Infiniteexact dimer GS

The triplon excitation spectrum, magnetisation plateaux (1/8, 1/4, 1/3) and large-Оұ intermediate / plaquette phases require quantities beyond a scalar ground-state energy and are tracked as a follow-up phase.

QAtlas.SherringtonKirkpatrick вҖ” Type
SherringtonKirkpatrick(; J::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Sherrington-Kirkpatrick mean-field Ising spin glass (Sherrington- Kirkpatrick 1975). The Hamiltonian is the canonical 1/вҲҡN random-Gaussian-coupling sum

H = -(1/вҲҡN) ОЈ_{i<j} J_ij Пғ_i Пғ_j,   J_ij ~ N(0, JВІ),

whose spin-glass transition lies at T_c = J.

QAtlas.SixVertex вҖ” Type
SixVertex(; a::Real = 1.0, b::Real = 1.0, c::Real = 1.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Classical six-vertex model on the infinite square lattice in the standard (a, b, c) parameterisation (Lieb 1967, Baxter 1982 ch. 8):

ПүвӮҒ = ПүвӮӮ = a,   ПүвӮғ = ПүвӮ„ = b,   ПүвӮ… = ПүвӮҶ = c

with the ice rule (each vertex has two incoming and two outgoing arrows). The single dimensionless invariant

О” = (aВІ + bВІ вҲ’ cВІ) / (2 a b)

selects the phase: О” > 1 ferroelectric (FE, frozen), |О”| < 1 disordered (Lieb / Sutherland 1967), О” < вҲ’1 antiferroelectric (AFE / F-model, Lieb 1967b).

Convenience constructors for the three classical sub-models (square_ice, f_model, kdp_model) are also provided.

Currently registered fetches:

QuantityBCCoverage
ResidualEntropyInfiniteSquare ice (О” = 1/2) + FE (О” > 1)
FreeEnergyInfiniteFE phase + square-ice point

The full disordered-phase free energy (Lieb / Sutherland 1967 trigonometric integral) and the AFE elliptic-function free energy (Lieb 1967b) are out of scope for the present commit (Phase 2 / Phase 3 of issue #163) and will throw an informative ArgumentError if requested.

See also: IsingSquare for the closest classical analog.

QAtlas.SpectralFormFactor вҖ” Type
SpectralFormFactor() <: AbstractQuantity

Disorder-averaged spectral form factor K(t) = вҹЁ|ОЈ_n e^{вҲ’iE_n t}|ВІвҹ© / ZВІ вҖ” the canonical late-time quantum-chaology diagnostic (Mehta 2004 В§16; Cotler et al. 2017).

For GUE random-matrix-theory eigenvalues in the large-N thermodynamic limit, with rescaled time П„ = t / N, the disorder-averaged SFF has the universal closed form

  • K(П„) = (П„/(2ПҖ)) вҲ’ (П„/(4ПҖ)) log|1 вҲ’ П„/(2ПҖ)| for П„ вүӨ 2ПҖ
  • K(П„) = 1 for П„ вүҘ 2ПҖ

so that K exhibits a linear ramp K(П„) вүҲ П„/ПҖ for small П„ and saturates to the universal plateau K(П„вҶ’вҲһ) = 1 for П„ beyond the Heisenberg time П„_H = 2ПҖ.

QAtlas Phase 1 (issue #243) exposes only the late-time plateau П„ вүҘ П„_H for the GUE ensemble; the ramp regime and the GOE/GSE sigma-model closed forms (Mehta 2004 В§16) are deferred to Phase 2.

References

  • M. L. Mehta, Random Matrices, 3rd ed., Elsevier (2004), В§16.
  • E. BrГ©zin, S. Hikami, Phys. Rev. E 55, 4067 (1997).
  • J. S. Cotler, G. Gur-Ari, M. Hanada, J. Polchinski, P. Saad, S. H. Shenker, D. Stanford, A. Streicher, M. Tezuka, JHEP 05, 118 (2017), arXiv:1611.04650 вҖ” ramp-plateau picture.

SpinGap() <: AbstractQuantity

Spin gap of an electron system,

О”_s = EвӮҖ(S^z = 1) - EвӮҖ(S^z = 0),

i.e. the lowest excitation energy at fixed total particle number that flips one spin. Zero whenever the spinon branch is gapless (e.g. the half-filled 1D Hubbard chain вҖ” rigorous LiebвҖ“Wu result), positive in a spin-gapped phase (Haldane chain, BCS superconductor, вҖҰ).

QAtlas.StringOrderParameter вҖ” Type
StringOrderParameter() <: AbstractQuantity

Kennedy-Tasaki non-local (string) order parameter

O_str = lim_{|i-j| -> infty} -<S^z_i exp[i pi sum_{i<k<j} S^z_k] S^z_j>

for S=1 chains. Detects the hidden Z2 x Z2 symmetry breaking that defines the Haldane phase (T. Kennedy and H. Tasaki, Phys. Rev. B 45, 304 (1992)). At the AKLT point the closed-form value is O_str = 4/9 (AKLT 1988), making it the canonical analytic test bed for any implementation that aims to detect topologically non-trivial gapped phases of integer-spin chains.

QAtlas.TightBindingChecksum вҖ” Type
TightBindingChecksum() <: AbstractQuantity

Sum of squared single-particle eigenvalues ОЈ О»бөўВІ of the tight-binding Bloch Hamiltonian, i.e. tr(HВІ). For a chiral (bipartite) lattice this equals 2 tВІ В· n_NN_bonds, an analytical identity independent of Lx, Ly, or k-grid details вҖ” a strong sanity invariant on top of the spectrum closed form.

source
QAtlas.TightBindingMaxEnergy вҖ” Type
TightBindingMaxEnergy() <: AbstractQuantity

Largest single-particle eigenvalue of the tight-binding Bloch Hamiltonian, i.e. max(О»бөў). For the chiral honeycomb this equals |t| В· max_k |f(k)| = 3|t| (saturated at the О“ point where the three nearest-neighbor phases add coherently), independent of Lx and Ly as long as the О“ point is on the discrete momentum grid (always true for PBC with Lx, Ly вүҘ 1).

Sister scalar to TightBindingChecksum (which captures ОЈО»бөўВІ = tr(HВІ) and is invariant under chiral pair sign-flips). The two together discriminate any single-eigenvalue perturbation: a sign error on a hopping displacement that flips a chiral pair changes neither the checksum nor the bandwidth at О“ only if it doesn't reach the О“ point вҖ” making them jointly sensitive to a broader class of typos.

QAtlas.TopologicalEntanglementEntropy вҖ” Type
TopologicalEntanglementEntropy() <: AbstractQuantity

Constant subleading correction Оі in the area-law bipartite entanglement entropy of a 2D topologically ordered ground state on a simply-connected disk region:

S(ПҒ_A) = Оұ |вҲӮA| вҲ’ Оі + O(|вҲӮA|вҒ»В№).

QAtlas.TopologicalInvariant вҖ” Type
TopologicalInvariant() <: AbstractQuantity

Topological Z_2 invariant of a 1D BdG superconductor (Kitaev 2001). Defined as the Pfaffian sign at the time-reversal-invariant momenta k = 0 and k = ПҖ,

\[\nu = \operatorname{sgn}\bigl[\operatorname{Pf}(H_{\mathrm{BdG}}(k=0)) \cdot \operatorname{Pf}(H_{\mathrm{BdG}}(k=\pi))\bigr] \in \{+1, -1\},\]

with ОҪ = -1 in the topological phase and ОҪ = +1 in the trivial phase. For a gapless bulk (Pfaffian zero at k = 0 or k = ПҖ) the invariant is ill-defined and implementations should signal an error.

Currently used by Kitaev1D.

QAtlas.VonNeumannEntropy вҖ” Type
VonNeumannEntropy{M}() <: AbstractQuantity
VonNeumannEntropy()                   # M = :equilibrium (default)
VonNeumannEntropy(:equilibrium)       # explicit equilibrium S(в„“)
VonNeumannEntropy(:quench)            # post-quench S(в„“, t)

Von Neumann entanglement entropy of a reduced density matrix, S_vN = вҲ’Tr ПҒ_A log ПҒ_A. The mode parameter M::Symbol is a phantom type that splits the dispatch into:

  • :equilibrium вҖ” equilibrium / thermal value S_vN = -Tr ПҒ_A log ПҒ_A of the GS or thermal reduced density matrix on the first в„“ sites (kwarg в„“). This is the original meaning; the no-argument constructor VonNeumannEntropy() keeps back-compatibility by routing here.

  • :quench вҖ” time-evolved entanglement entropy S_vN(в„“, t) = -Tr ПҒ_A(t) log ПҒ_A(t) after a sudden quench from the ground state of an initial::AbstractQAtlasModel (H_0) to the post-quench Hamiltonian (the model argument to fetch). CalabreseвҖ“Cardy quasi-particle picture (J. Stat. Mech. P04010 (2005)): linear growth S(в„“, t) вүҲ (c/3) v_E t for t вүӘ в„“/(2 v_E), saturating at (c/3) log в„“ + const for t вү« в„“/(2 v_E).

See docs/src/calc/tfim-quench-entanglement.md for the free-fermion derivation in the TFIM.

QAtlas.WZWSU2 вҖ” Type
WZWSU2(k::Int) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

WessвҖ“ZuminoвҖ“Witten model with affine Lie algebra SU(2) at level k вүҘ 1. Construction throws DomainError for k вүӨ 0.

Special cases:

  • k = 1: c = 1 (free boson at the SU(2)-symmetric radius; low-energy theory of the spin-1/2 Heisenberg antiferromagnet, Affleck 1989).
  • k = 2: c = 3/2 вҖ” equivalent to 3 free Majorana fermions (each contributing c = 1/2), or equivalently the smallest N=1 super-Virasoro minimal model. Note that "Ising Г— free Majorana" with one Majorana would only give c = 1/2 + 1/2 = 1 вү  3/2; the correct decomposition needs three Majorana fermions.
  • k = 3: c = 9/5.
fetch(WZWSU2(1), CentralCharge())                    # 1//1
fetch(WZWSU2(1), ConformalWeights(); j=1//2)         # 1//4

See also: MinimalModel, Universality, CentralCharge, ConformalWeights.

QAtlas.XXZ1D вҖ” Type
XXZ1D(; J::Real = 1.0, О”::Real = 0.0) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

  • E. Lieb, T. Schultz, D. Mattis, Annals Phys. 16, 407 (1961).
  • P. Pfeuty, Annals Phys. 57, 79 (1970).
  • S. Sachdev, Quantum Phase Transitions (2nd ed., CUP 2011), В§2.

QAtlas.YangLee вҖ” Type
YangLee() <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Yang-Lee CFT вҖ” the non-unitary Virasoro minimal model M(5, 2) describing the universality class of the Lee-Yang edge singularity (Yang-Lee 1952; Cardy 1985).

The model has no continuous parameters: M(5, 2) is fixed.

Quantities registered (Phase 1):

QuantityBCMethod
CentralChargeInfinitedelegated to MinimalModel(5,2)
ConformalWeightsInfinitedelegated to MinimalModel(5,2)

The famous negative-dimension primary h_{1,2} = -1/5 is the edge exponent and is what makes the theory non-unitary (c = -22/5 < 0).

References

  • C. N. Yang and T. D. Lee, Phys. Rev. 87, 404 (1952).
  • J. L. Cardy, Phys. Rev. Lett. 54, 1354 (1985).

QAtlas.ZnParafermion вҖ” Type
ZnParafermion(; n::Integer=3) <: AbstractQAtlasModel

Zn parafermion CFT (Fateev-Zamolodchikov 1985), the SU(2)n / U(1) coset conformal field theory with central charge c = 2(n-1)/(n+2).

The default n = 3 selects the Z_3 parafermion = 3-state Potts critical CFT with c = 4/5.

Arguments

  • n::Integer = 3 вҖ” parafermion level; must satisfy n вүҘ 2.

Examples

QAtlas.fetch(ZnParafermion(; n=2), CentralCharge(), Infinite())  # 1//2  (Ising)
QAtlas.fetch(ZnParafermion(; n=3), CentralCharge(), Infinite())  # 4//5  (3-state Potts)
QAtlas.fetch(ZnParafermion(; n=4), CentralCharge(), Infinite())  # 1//1  (free boson)
QAtlas.fetch(ZnParafermion(; n=5), CentralCharge(), Infinite())  # 8//7

References

  • V. A. Fateev, A. B. Zamolodchikov, Sov. Phys. JETP 62, 215 (1985).

QAtlas._free_energy_fe вҖ” Method
_free_energy_fe(a, b, c) -> Float64

Closed-form free-energy density of the six-vertex model in the ferroelectric phase О” > 1 (Lieb 1967c, Baxter 1982 В§8.10):

f = вҲ’log max(a, b)

The ground state is the unique frozen configuration with all arrows parallel along the favoured axis, so the partition function is dominated by (max(a,b))^N and the free energy density is вҲ’log of the larger weight. At the KDP point (a > 2, b = c = 1) this reduces to вҲ’log a.

source
QAtlas._heisenberg_szz_muller вҖ” Method
_heisenberg_szz_muller(J, q, Пү) -> Float64

MГјller-ansatz approximation to the longitudinal dynamic structure factor S^{zz}(q, Пү) of the spin-ВҪ XXX AFM chain. The closed-form expression, valid inside the two-spinon continuum, is

S^{zz}(q, Пү) вүҲ  Оҳ[Пү - Оө_L(q)] В· Оҳ[Оө_U(q) - Пү]
                ----------------------------------
                    2 вҲҡ(ПүВІ - Оө_L(q)ВІ)

with Оө_L(q) = (ПҖ J / 2) |sin q| and Оө_U(q) = ПҖ J |sin(q/2)|. Outside the closed continuum (i.e. Пү вүӨ Оө_L or Пү вүҘ Оө_U) the expression returns exactly 0.0.

The square-root singularity at the lower edge is integrable, so we return the raw analytical value (no regulator); callers performing Пү-integrals are expected to use a routine that handles the integrable singularity (e.g. GaussвҖ“Chebyshev or substitution ПүВІ = Оө_LВІ + s).

This is Phase 1 вҖ” the MГјller ansatz captures the lower-edge behaviour and the support correctly but mis-estimates the spectral weight near the upper edge. The Phase 2 exact result is given by the CauxвҖ“Hagemans (2006) algebraic Bethe ansatz form factor sum; implementing it is tracked as a TODO in docs/src/calc/heisenberg-spinons.md.

Longitudinal only вҖ” S^{xx}, S^{yy} are NOT equal to S^{zz} at q вү  0

Despite the SU(2) symmetry of the spin-ВҪ XXX AFM chain, the individual transverse and longitudinal dynamic structure factors S^{xx}(q, Пү) = S^{yy}(q, Пү) and S^{zz}(q, Пү) differ at any q вү  0 вҖ” only their sum (the rotation-invariant trace ОЈ_Оұ S^{ОұОұ}) is equal across spin axes. The transverse MГјller- style ansatz (Schulz 1986; Bougourzi-Karbach-MГјller 1998) shares the two-spinon support [Оө_L(q), Оө_U(q)] but has a different singularity structure at the lower edge. This method returns only the longitudinal S^{zz}; do not use it as a drop-in for S^{xx} at finite q.

source
QAtlas._hubbard1d_charge_gap вҖ” Method
_hubbard1d_charge_gap(t, U) -> Float64

LiebвҖ“Wu (1968) Mott (charge) gap at half filling:

О”_c = (16 tВІ / U) вҲ«_1^вҲһ dПү  вҲҡ(ПүВІ - 1) / sinh(2ПҖ t Пү / U).

The integrand vanishes at Пү = 1 like вҲҡ(Пү-1) and decays exponentially at large Пү; quadgk resolves both endpoints with the default GaussвҖ“Kronrod adaptive subdivision.

QAtlas._ising_sq_transfer_matrix вҖ” Method
_ising_sq_transfer_matrix(Ly, ОІ, J) -> Matrix

Return the 2^Ly Г— 2^Ly symmetric transfer matrix for a row of Ly Ising spins with PBC along the row direction.

The symmetric (Hermitian) form is defined by:

T_{Пғ,Пғ'} = exp(ОІJ/2 В· EвӮ•(Пғ)) В· exp(ОІJ В· EбөҘ(Пғ,Пғ')) В· exp(ОІJ/2 В· EвӮ•(Пғ'))

where EвӮ•(Пғ) = ОЈвұјвӮҢвӮҒ^Ly Пғвұј Пғ_{(j mod Ly)+1} (horizontal bonds within row, PBC) EбөҘ(Пғ,Пғ') = ОЈвұјвӮҢвӮҒ^Ly Пғвұј Пғ'вұј (vertical bonds between rows)

Note: for Ly = 2, each horizontal bond is counted twice by the PBC sum (ПғвӮҒПғвӮӮ + ПғвӮӮПғвӮҒ = 2ПғвӮҒПғвӮӮ). The same applies along the transfer direction: tr(T^Lx) double-counts the vertical bonds when Lx = 2, because the cyclic product T[Пғ,Пғ'] T[Пғ',Пғ] weights the single pair of rows with the vertical Boltzmann factor twice. This doubling is an intrinsic property of the PBC transfer-matrix formula at L = 2 and is used consistently by the brute-force cross-check in test/util/classical_partition.jl (its bond list is constructed to match this convention by enumerating (i, j) вҶ” (i, (j mod Ly) + 1) and (i, j) вҶ” ((i mod Lx) + 1, j) for every site).

The function is generic in ОІ and J so that automatic-differentiation dual numbers (e.g. ForwardDiff.Dual) propagate through the matrix elements. The element type of the returned matrix is inferred from typeof(exp(ОІ * J)).

source
QAtlas._kitaev1d_bdg_spectrum вҖ” Method
_kitaev1d_bdg_spectrum(N, Ој, t, О”) -> Vector{Float64}

Return the N non-negative BdG quasiparticle energies of the OBC Kitaev1D chain with N sites and parameters (Ој, t, О”).

The BdG matrix in Nambu basis is H_BdG = [[A, B]; [-B, -A]] (the same real, antisymmetric 2N Г— 2N convention used by _tfim_bdg_spectrum), with

A_{ii}   = -Ој
A_{i,i+1} = A_{i+1,i} = -t
B_{i,i+1} = +О”,  B_{i+1,i} = -О”.

Eigenvalues come in Вұ pairs; the function returns the non-negative half, sorted ascending. The BdG zero modes of the topological phase (lifted by exponentially small NвҒ»В№ corrections) appear as the smallest entry.

This is a strict generalisation of _tfim_bdg_spectrum: at (Ој, t, О”) = (-2h, J, J) the matrix coincides with the TFIM BdG matrix and the returned spectrum matches _tfim_bdg_spectrum(N, J, h).

source
QAtlas._kitaev1d_majorana_bloch вҖ” Method
_kitaev1d_majorana_bloch(Ој, t, k::Symbol) -> Matrix{Float64}

Return the 2 Г— 2 real antisymmetric Majorana Bloch matrix A(k) of the infinite Kitaev1D chain at the time-reversal-invariant momenta k вҲҲ {:zero, :pi}. At those momenta the pairing amplitude 2О” sin k vanishes, so the matrix depends only on Ој and t:

A(k=0)  = [ 0  Ој + 2t; -(Ој + 2t)  0 ]   вҮ’   Pf A(k=0)  = Ој + 2t
A(k=ПҖ)  = [ 0  Ој - 2t; -(Ој - 2t)  0 ]   вҮ’   Pf A(k=ПҖ)  = Ој - 2t

(Convention: the diagonal Majorana Bloch matrix at TR-invariant momenta has off-diagonal entry equal to the on-site mass term Ој + 2t cos k.) This is the matrix on which the Kitaev (2001) ZвӮӮ Pfaffian invariant is evaluated.

QAtlas._kitaev_pbc_sector_energy вҖ” Method
_kitaev_pbc_sector_energy(m, Lx, Ly, ОҪx, ОҪy) -> Float64

Per-site ground state energy on the Lx Г— Ly torus within a fixed topological flux sector (ОҪx, ОҪy) вҲҲ {0, 1/2}ВІ. ОҪx = 1/2 flips every bond that crosses the m1 = Lx вҶ’ m1 = 1 seam (anti-periodic fermion boundary condition along the x-direction); ОҪy = 1/2 does the same in the y-direction. The four sectors correspond to the four inequivalent choices (W_x, W_y) вҲҲ {Вұ1}ВІ of the two non-contractible Wilson-loop operators.

Built as a singular-value decomposition of the Majorana hopping matrix M with entries ВұK_Оі, where the sign flips whenever a bond of type Оі crosses one of the selected seams. Per-site energy = вҲ’ОЈ Пғ_k / (2В·LxВ·Ly).

source
QAtlas._kitaev_thermo_infinite вҖ” Method
_kitaev_thermo_infinite(quantity, model, ОІ; rtol) -> Float64

Per-site matter-sector thermodynamic potential of the infinite Kitaev honeycomb at inverse temperature ОІ. quantity is one of (:free_energy, :entropy, :specific_heat, :energy).

The integrals are evaluated via adaptive Gauss-Kronrod quadrature over the BZ (see _kitaev_bz_integral). The leading factor 1/(2В·(2ПҖ)ВІ) accounts for the per-site (two sublattice atoms) and the 2D BZ volume.

source
QAtlas._kitaev_thermo_obc вҖ” Method
_kitaev_thermo_obc(quantity, model, Lx, Ly, ОІ) -> Float64

Per-site matter-sector thermodynamic potential of the Lx Г— Ly OBC honeycomb strip at inverse temperature ОІ, computed by summing each BdG positive Majorana mode's contribution.

The bipartite hopping matrix M = _obc_hopping_matrix(model, Lx, Ly) has LxВ·Ly positive singular values Пғ_k; the lattice carries N_sites = 2В·LxВ·Ly sites, so per-site potentials scale as (1/(2В·LxВ·Ly)) ОЈ_k g(Пғ_k) with g the free-fermion-mode kernel.

source
QAtlas._majorana_covariance_gs вҖ” Method
_majorana_covariance_gs(h::AbstractMatrix) -> Matrix{Float64}

Ground-state Majorana covariance ОЈ of a quadratic Hamiltonian whose Majorana matrix is h. ОЈ is real antisymmetric, with вҹЁОі_a Оі_bвҹ©_GS = Оҙ_{ab} + i ОЈ_{ab}. The formula ОЈ = -i В· sign(i h) is used, evaluated through an eigendecomposition of the Hermitian matrix i h.

QAtlas._majorana_ham вҖ” Method
_majorana_ham(N, J, h) -> Matrix{Float64}

Return the 2N Г— 2N real antisymmetric Majorana Hamiltonian matrix h of the OBC TFIM such that H = (i/4) ОЈ h_{ab} Оі_a Оі_b.

source
QAtlas._majorana_thermal_covariance вҖ” Method
_majorana_thermal_covariance(h::AbstractMatrix, ОІ::Real) -> Matrix{Float64}

Thermal-equilibrium Majorana covariance at inverse temperature ОІ. The T = 0 ground-state formula ОЈ_GS = -i sign(i h) generalises to

ОЈ(ОІ) = -i tanh((ОІ/2) В· i h)

so that вҹЁОі_a Оі_bвҹ©_ОІ = Оҙ_{ab} + i ОЈ(ОІ)_{ab}. In the canonical 2Г—2 BdG block this gives the off-diagonal entry tanh(ОІОӣ/2), recovering the FermiвҖ“Dirac population of each quasiparticle and reducing to Вұ1 as ОІ вҶ’ вҲһ.

ОІ = Inf falls back to _majorana_covariance_gs.

source
QAtlas._obc_hopping_matrix вҖ” Method
_obc_hopping_matrix(model, Lx, Ly) -> Matrix{Float64}

LxВ·Ly Г— LxВ·Ly bipartite hopping matrix for the flux-free-sector Majorana problem with open boundary conditions in both lattice directions. M[a, b] = K_Оі whenever the A-sublattice site of unit cell a connects to the B-sublattice site of unit cell b via a bond of type Оі (matching Lattice2D's Honeycomb topology conventions: type1 вҶ” Kz within the same cell, type2 вҶ” Kx crossing (+aвӮҒ, вҲ’aвӮӮ), type3 вҶ” Ky crossing (вҲ’aвӮӮ)). Bonds that would leave the Lx Г— Ly strip are dropped.

Row indexing: a = (m1 вҲ’ 1) Ly + m2 for (m1, m2) вҲҲ 1..Lx Г— 1..Ly.

source
QAtlas._onsager_log_z_per_site вҖ” Method
_onsager_log_z_per_site(K) -> Float64

Onsager (1944) thermodynamic-limit log Z / N = -ОІf per site of the classical 2D Ising model on the square lattice, parameterised by the reduced coupling K = ОІJ. The bond-counting convention matches _ising_sq_transfer_matrix(Lx, Ly, ОІ, J) (each bond enumerated once for Lx, Ly вүҘ 3):

-ОІ f(K) = log(2) + (1/(2ПҖ)) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dПҶ В· log[(A(ПҶ) + вҲҡ(A(ПҶ)ВІ вҲ’ BВІ))/2]
A(ПҶ)    = coshВІ(2K) вҲ’ sinh(2K) В· cos(ПҶ),
B       = sinh(2K).

The integrand is finite for all K вүҘ 0 (A вүҘ B strictly except at the critical point K_c = ln(1+вҲҡ2)/2, where A вҲ’ B вҶ’ 0 at ПҶ = 0). QuadGK's adaptive quadrature handles the integrable square-root edge without intervention.

Reference: L. Onsager, Phys. Rev. 65, 117 (1944), Eq. (105).

source

# ПғЛЈ at site 3 in an N=5 chain:
_pauli_string(5, 3 => _Пғx)

source
QAtlas._peschel_mode_entropy вҖ” Method
_peschel_mode_entropy(ОҪ::Float64) -> Float64

Per-mode von Neumann entropy

s(ОҪ) = -[(1-ОҪ)/2 В· ln((1-ОҪ)/2) + (1+ОҪ)/2 В· ln((1+ОҪ)/2)]

as a function of the Majorana covariance singular value ОҪ вҲҲ [0, 1]. Numerically stable at ОҪ вҶ’ 0 (s вҶ’ ln 2) and ОҪ вҶ’ 1 (s вҶ’ 0).

source
QAtlas._peschel_mode_renyi вҖ” Method
_peschel_mode_renyi(ОҪ::Real, Оұ::Real) -> Float64

Per-mode RГ©nyi entropy of order Оұ (Оұ вү  1) for a Gaussian fermionic mode with covariance singular value ОҪ вҲҲ [0, 1]:

s_Оұ(ОҪ) = (1 / (1 - Оұ)) В· log[ ((1+ОҪ)/2)^Оұ + ((1-ОҪ)/2)^Оұ ].

Numerically stable at the corner cases:

  • ОҪ вҶ’ 1 (pure mode): the vanishing branch is dropped rather than clamped to eps(Float64) вҖ” clamping injects an Оұ В· log(eps) error that becomes visible at small Оұ < 1 (the dominant branch is Оұ log 1 вүҲ 0, so a clamped contribution of exp(Оұ log eps) no longer underflows). See test/models/test_TFIM_renyi.jl "Compare against full ED".
  • ОҪ вҶ’ 0 (maximally mixed): both branches are (1/2)^Оұ, giving s_Оұ = log(2^{1-Оұ}) / (1 вҲ’ Оұ) = log 2.
  • Оұ вҶ’ вҲһ: s_Оұ вҶ’ -log p_max = -log((1+ОҪ)/2) (min-entropy limit).
  • Оұ вҶ’ 0вҒә: s_Оұ вҶ’ log 2 (Hartley entropy for a 2-level Bernoulli).
source

QAtlas._s1_partial_trace_A вҖ” Method
_s1_partial_trace_A(ПҒ::AbstractMatrix, в„“::Int, N::Int) -> Matrix{ComplexF64}

Trace out sites в„“+1 .. N of the 3^N Г— 3^N density matrix ПҒ and return the 3^в„“ Г— 3^в„“ reduced density matrix on sites 1 .. в„“ (local dimension d = 3 for spin-1).

The convention matches _spin1_string: site 1 is the leftmost (slowest- running) tensor factor, so the row/column index decomposes as (i_A, i_B) with i_A = 0:dA-1, i_B = 0:dB-1 where dA = d^в„“, dB = d^(N-в„“). Reshaping ПҒ as (dA, dB, dA, dB) and contracting the B indices then gives ПҒ_A.

source
QAtlas._s1_thermal_kernel вҖ” Method
_s1_thermal_kernel(model, N, beta) -> NamedTuple

Compute the eigendecomposition of the OBC spin-1 Heisenberg Hamiltonian on N sites and return everything downstream observables need to evaluate thermal expectation values:

  • H вҖ” the dense 3^N Г— 3^N Hermitian Hamiltonian matrix
  • evals вҖ” sorted real eigenvalues (F.values)
  • evecs вҖ” eigenvector matrix (F.vectors)
  • weights вҖ” Boltzmann weights wвӮҷ = exp(-ОІ(eвӮҷ - emin))/ZМғ, normalised so sum(weights) == 1
  • ПҒ вҖ” evecs В· diagm(weights) В· evecs', the thermal density matrix in the computational (product) basis

For beta = Inf we collapse onto the (possibly degenerate) ground-state manifold by zeroing all weights above evals[1] + 1e-12.

Constructed once per fetch call (so a routine that needs both an energy and a magnetisation does not pay for two eigen calls). No caching across calls вҖ” that would require a per-model mutable cache and hasn't been profiled to matter yet.

QAtlas._sz_sz_corr вҖ” Method
_sz_sz_corr(N, J, h, i, j, t; ОІ = Inf) -> ComplexF64

вҹЁПғб¶»_i(t) Пғб¶»_j(0)вҹ©_ОІ for the OBC TFIM at inverse temperature ОІ (default Inf вҮ’ ground state).

QAtlas._tfim_bdg_diagonalise вҖ” Method
_tfim_bdg_diagonalise(N, J, h) -> (Оӣ::Vector{Float64}, П•::Matrix{Float64}, ПҲ::Matrix{Float64})

Diagonalise the OBC BdG matrix of the TFIM with N sites, returning the N positive quasiparticle energies Оӣn and the corresponding particle / hole amplitudes (П•n, ПҲ_n) вҲҲ в„қ^N (Lieb-Schultz-Mattis convention).

The Bogoliubov quasiparticles are

О·_n = ОЈ_i [ (П•_n,i + ПҲ_n,i)/2 c_i + (П•_n,i вҲ’ ПҲ_n,i)/2 c_i^вҖ  ]

so the orthogonal (N + N) Г— (2N) Bogoliubov transformation has rows (g_n; h_n) = ((П•_n + ПҲ_n)/2, (П•_n вҲ’ ПҲ_n)/2).

source
QAtlas._tfim_bdg_full вҖ” Method
_tfim_bdg_full(N, J, h) -> (Оӣ::Vector{Float64}, U::Matrix{Float64}, V::Matrix{Float64})

Full diagonalisation of the 2N Г— 2N TFIM OBC BdG Hamiltonian. Returns the N positive quasiparticle energies Оӣ[n] and the Bogoliubov amplitudes U[i, n], V[i, n] (site-index i, mode-index n) defining

О·_n = ОЈбөў U[i, n] cбөў + V[i, n] cбөўвҖ ,

normalised by ОЈбөў (U[i, n]ВІ + V[i, n]ВІ) = 1.

The 2N Г— 2N BdG matrix is H_BdG = [A B; -B -A] with A symmetric (transverse field + hopping) and B antisymmetric (pairing); its spectrum is symmetric about zero by particle-hole symmetry. We pick the N eigenvectors with positive eigenvalues; for each such eigenvector (x, y) вҲҲ в„қВІбҙә, we identify U[:, n] = x, V[:, n] = y.

Diagonalising the full 2N Г— 2N matrix (rather than the squared N Г— N system (AвҲ’B)(A+B) ПҶ = ОӣВІ ПҶ) is robust to the near-zero edge mode in the ordered phase (h < J), which becomes Оӣ вүҲ 10вҒ»В№вҒө and renders the ПҲ = (A+B)ПҶ / Оӣ reconstruction ill-conditioned at certain N.

source
QAtlas._tfim_bdg_spectrum вҖ” Method
_tfim_bdg_spectrum(N, J, h) -> Vector{Float64}

Return the N positive BdG quasiparticle energies ОӣвӮҷ > 0 for the OBC TFIM with N sites, Ising coupling J, and transverse field h.

The 2NГ—2N BdG matrix is: H_BdG = [[A, B]; [-B, -A]] where A (tridiagonal, symmetric) encodes hopping + onsite energy, and B (antisymmetric) encodes the pairing terms from JW transformation.

A_{ii}   = 2h
A_{i,iВұ1} = -J
B_{i,i+1} = +J,  B_{i+1,i} = -J
source
QAtlas._tfim_cc_entanglement вҖ” Method
_tfim_cc_entanglement(J, h, в„“, ОІ; Оұ=1.0) -> Float64

Calabrese-Cardy closed form for the RГ©nyi-Оұ entanglement entropy of a contiguous block of length в„“ in the infinite TFIM at inverse temperature ОІ (use ОІ = Inf for the ground state).

The Ising central charge c = 1/2 is hard-coded; the prefactor

P_Оұ = (c / 6) В· (1 + 1/Оұ)

reduces to c/3 at Оұ = 1 (von Neumann) and to (c/6)(1 + 1/Оұ) otherwise. At criticality (h вүҲ J) the gapped form is replaced by its Оҫ вҶ’ вҲһ limit log(2 в„“) (T = 0) or log[(ОІ/ПҖ) sinh(ПҖ в„“ / ОІ)] (T > 0).

Returns the leading-log term only вҖ” the non-universal additive constant S_0 is dropped, so downstream fits should include an offset.

Off-critical at finite ОІ requires composing the gapped CC mass with the thermal CFT scaling and is not implemented here.

source
QAtlas._tfim_chi_F_infinite вҖ” Method
_tfim_chi_F_infinite(J, h; rtol=1e-10) -> Float64

Per-site fidelity susceptibility ПҮ_F / L for the infinite TFIM with respect to the transverse field h, computed by GaussвҖ“Kronrod quadrature of the closed-form Bogoliubov-vacuum overlap integral

ПҮ_F / L = (1 / 8ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ (J sin k)ВІ / Оө_k(h)вҒҙ dk,
Оө_k(h)  = вҲҡ(JВІ + hВІ вҲ’ 2 J h cos k) = Оӣ_k(h) / 2.

Equivalent to (2/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ (J sin k)ВІ / Оӣ_k(h)вҒҙ dk if expressed in terms of the doubled BdG dispersion Оӣ_k = 2 Оө_k.

The closed form ПҮ_F / L = JВІ / (8 (JВІ - hВІ)ВІ) (h вү  J) follows by residue integration; the routine still does numerical quadrature so that small numerical errors propagate consistently with the OBC counterpart and so that the implementation is robust to future generalisations (e.g. ПҮ_F with respect to J).

Throws DomainError at the critical point h = J (logarithmic divergence of the integrand at k = 0).

source
QAtlas._tfim_chi_F_obc вҖ” Method
_tfim_chi_F_obc(N, J, h) -> Float64

Total fidelity susceptibility (NOT per site) of the OBC TFIM with N sites, with respect to the transverse field h.

Formula (2nd-order perturbation theory on the BdG diagonalisation):

ПҮ_F = ОЈ_{p < q} 4 X_{pq}ВІ / (Оӣ_p + Оӣ_q)ВІ,
X_{pq} = ОЈвұј [U_{q,j} V_{p,j} вҲ’ U_{p,j} V_{q,j}],

where U[j, n], V[j, n] are the Bogoliubov particle/hole amplitudes returned by _tfim_bdg_full.

Cost: O(NВі) eigendecomposition + O(NВі) for the X matrix + O(NВІ) summation.

source
QAtlas._tfim_chi_imag_zz_dynamic_proxy вҖ” Method
_tfim_chi_imag_zz_dynamic_proxy(J, h, ОІ, q, Пү, N_proxy, t_max, dt) -> Float64

OBC large-N proxy implementation of the imaginary part of the dynamic longitudinal susceptibility ПҮ''_zz(q, Пү; ОІ). Used by the Infinite() fetch router; the heavy lifting lives here so the public method stays a thin wrapper.

The Kubo formula (Kubo 1957; Mahan, Many-Particle Physics, ch. 3) gives the spectral function as the time-Fourier transform of the expectation value of the commutator,

ПҮ''_zz(q, Пү; ОІ) = (1/2) вҲ«dt e^{iПүt} В· (1/N_b) ОЈ_{i,j вҲҲ bulk}
                      e^{-iq(i-j)} вҹЁ[Пғб¶»_i(t), Пғб¶»_j(0)]вҹ©_ОІ.

For Hermitian operators in a thermal state Hermiticity gives

вҹЁ[Пғб¶»_i(t), Пғб¶»_j(0)]вҹ©_ОІ = 2i Im вҹЁПғб¶»_i(t) Пғб¶»_j(0)вҹ©_ОІ,

so each (i, j, t) point reuses the cached Pfaffian correlator _sz_sz_corr_from_cached and only the imaginary part participates. The result is real (the explicit i from the commutator combines with the (1/2) and the imaginary part to give a real spectral function); we return real(...) defensively against round-off.

Discretisation: t вҲҲ [-t_max, t_max] with spacing dt, (i, j) restricted to the central bulk window [N/4, 3N/4] of an N_proxy-site OBC chain. The Majorana Hamiltonian and thermal covariance are computed once; the evolution matrix R(t) is recomputed at every time step (single 2N Г— 2N expm) вҖ” same machinery as _tfim_zz_structure_factor_dynamic_proxy.

source
QAtlas._tfim_dispersion вҖ” Method
_tfim_dispersion(k, J, h) -> Float64

Single-particle BdG quasiparticle energy at momentum k for the TFIM with couplings J (Z-Z coupling) and h (transverse field):

Оӣ(k) = 2 вҲҡ(JВІ + hВІ - 2 J h cos k).

QAtlas._tfim_gge_energy_density вҖ” Method
_tfim_gge_energy_density(J, h0, hf) -> Float64

Per-site GGE energy density of the post-quench TFIM (J, hf) starting from the ground state of (J, h0):

Оө_GGE = -(1/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk В· (Оӣ_k(hf) / 2) В· (1 вҲ’ 2 n_k(h0, hf))

with Оӣ_k(h) = 2 вҲҡ(JВІ + hВІ вҲ’ 2 J h cos k) and n_k = sinВІ(Оё_k(h0) вҲ’ Оё_k(hf)).

Sanity:

  • h0 == hf вҮ’ n_k вүЎ 0 вҮ’ Оө_GGE = -(1/ПҖ) вҲ« Оӣ/2 dk = Оө_GS(hf).

The integral is evaluated via adaptive Gauss-Kronrod quadrature with rtol = 1e-10.

source
QAtlas._tfim_gge_magnetization_x вҖ” Method
_tfim_gge_magnetization_x(J, h0, hf) -> Float64

Per-site GGE transverse magnetisation вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©_GGE of the post-quench TFIM (J, hf) starting from the ground state of (J, h0):

вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©_GGE = (2/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk В· (hf вҲ’ J cos k)/Оӣ_k(hf) В· (1 вҲ’ 2 n_k)

The factor (hf вҲ’ J cos k)/Оӣ_k(hf) equals cos(2 Оё_k(hf)) / 2, so equivalently

вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©_GGE = (1/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk В· cos(2 Оё_k(hf)) В· (1 вҲ’ 2 n_k).

We use the explicit (hf - J cos k)/Оӣ_k form to share the integrand structure with the equilibrium MagnetizationX routine in TFIM_thermal.jl.

Sanity:

  • h0 == hf вҮ’ n_k вүЎ 0 вҮ’ recovers the T = 0 / ОІ = вҲһ equilibrium value (2/ПҖ) вҲ« (h вҲ’ J cos k)/Оӣ_k dk.
source
QAtlas._tfim_gge_occupation вҖ” Method
_tfim_gge_occupation(k, J, h0, hf) -> Float64

Conserved mode occupation n_k = sinВІ((Оё_k(h0) вҲ’ Оё_k(hf))) generated by a sudden quench from initial transverse field h0 to final transverse field hf at momentum k.

Numerical detail: О”(2Оё) = 2Оё_k(h0) вҲ’ 2Оё_k(hf) is computed via the two-argument atan (atan2) for branch safety; we then divide by 2 inside sin to get Оё_k(h0) вҲ’ Оё_k(hf).

source
QAtlas._tfim_gge_two_theta вҖ” Method
_tfim_gge_two_theta(k, J, h) -> Float64

The Bogoliubov double-angle 2 Оё_k(h) of the TFIM at momentum k,

2 Оё_k(h) = atan2(J sin k, h вҲ’ J cos k) вҲҲ (-ПҖ, ПҖ].

The atan2 form keeps the angle on the principal branch through the critical point h = J and through k = 0, ПҖ, which a naive atan(J sin k / (h - J cos k)) misses (the denominator changes sign).

source
QAtlas._tfim_loschmidt_obc_log_echo вҖ” Method
_tfim_loschmidt_obc_log_echo(N, J, h0, hf, t) -> Float64

Compute log L(t) for the OBC TFIM quench h0 вҶ’ hf at finite N.

Implementation: diagonalise BdG of H0 and Hf, build the rotation matrix between their Bogoliubov bases, and evaluate the per-mode Loschmidt product.

Concretely, the Bogoliubov transformations relate fermion operators to quasiparticles as

О·_n = ОЈ_i ( g_n,i c_i + h_n,i c_i^вҖ  ),

with the two row matrices G = (П• + ПҲ)/2, H = (П• вҲ’ ПҲ)/2. The vacuum overlap of H0 and Hf Bogoliubov vacua decomposes into a per-mode product whose factors are

cosВІ Оё_n + sinВІ Оё_n e^{-2 i Оӣ_n^{(f)} t}

with cosВІ Оёn = ОЈm |P^{(+)}{n,m}|ВІ, sinВІ Оёn = ОЈm |P^{(-)}{n,m}|ВІ, where

P^{(+)} = G^{(f)} G^{(0)вҖ } + H^{(f)} H^{(0)вҖ }
P^{(-)} = G^{(f)} H^{(0)вҖ } + H^{(f)} G^{(0)вҖ }.

In the diagonal-pair limit (translationally invariant), this reduces to the issue's (cosВІО”Оё_k + sinВІО”Оё_k e^{-2iОӣ_k t}) factor; for OBC the row-norm form folds residual mode mixing into per-mode angles consistent with unitarity (cosВІ + sinВІ = 1 is enforced by row normalisation).

OBC implementation is a per-mode-product approximation, not the exact Pfaffian

The exact OBC Bogoliubov-vacuum overlap is a Pfaffian (or determinant) of the full (N + N) Г— (N + N) BdG mode-mixing matrix between the H0 and Hf bases вҖ” equivalent to the Onishi-Yoshida formula or Robledo's Pfaffian sign-resolved form for HFB vacua. The implementation here uses the diagonal (rank-1-per-row) approximation: each Hf mode n is summed against all H0 modes m only via the row norms ОЈ_m |P^{(Вұ)}_{n,m}|ВІ, folding off-diagonal mode-mixing structure into per-mode angles consistent with unitarity. This is exact in the translationally- invariant (PBC, k-decoupled) limit and converges to the exact Pfaffian as N вҶ’ вҲһ at OBC, but at any finite N it carries an O(off-diagonal mode-mixing / N) discrepancy from the strict Pfaffian value. The cross-check test OBC N вҶ’ вҲһ matches Infinite (off-cusp) uses a 0.20 tolerance to accommodate this; a tighter assertion (e.g. <0.02 at N = 128) would expose the approximation. Replacing this with the Pfaffian form is a Phase 2 candidate if precision is needed at modest N.

Returns log L(t), suitable for direct О» = вҲ’log L / N conversion.

source

QAtlas._tfim_pbc_mass_gap вҖ” Method
_tfim_pbc_mass_gap(N, J, h) -> Float64

Lowest single excitation energy of the N-site PBC TFIM.

The Hilbert space splits by ZвӮӮ parity P = вҲҸбөў ПғЛЈбөў:

  • even parity (NS): GS energy -ВҪ ОЈ_k Оӣ_k, lowest excited state is a pair of quasiparticles вҶ’ minimum two-particle energy is Оӣ_{kвӮҒ} + Оӣ_{kвӮӮ} over the two smallest NS Оӣ's.
  • odd parity (R): GS energy -ВҪ ОЈ_k Оӣ_k, lowest excited state is a single quasiparticle вҶ’ minimum one-particle energy is min_k Оӣ_k^R.

The mass gap is min(E_excited) вҲ’ min(E_GS) across both sectors.

QAtlas._tfim_pfeuty_mz вҖ” Method
_tfim_pfeuty_mz(J, h) -> Float64

Pfeuty (1970) closed-form spontaneous longitudinal magnetisation per site for the infinite TFIM at T = 0 (Pauli convention, eigenvalues Вұ1):

m_z = (1 - (h/J)ВІ)^{1/8}    (h < J, ordered phase)
    = 0                     (h вүҘ J, disordered phase)

The exponent ОІ = 1/8 is the OnsagerвҖ“Yang exponent of the 2D Ising universality class.

Returns the positive branch of the spontaneously-broken ZвӮӮ doublet (the negative branch is -m_z). m_z = 0 exactly at the critical point h = J.

QAtlas._tfim_sigma_x_quench_infinite вҖ” Method
_tfim_sigma_x_quench_infinite(J, h_0, h_f, t) -> Float64

Closed-form integral

вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©(t) = (1/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk [
             cos(2 Оё_k^f) В· cos(2 О”Оё_k)
           + sin(2 Оё_k^f) В· sin(2 О”Оё_k) В· cos(2 Оӣ_k^f t) ]

with О”Оёk = Оёk(hf) вҲ’ Оёk(h0) for the infinite TFIM after a sudden quench h0 вҶ’ h_f at fixed J. Adaptive GaussвҖ“Kronrod quadrature with rtol = 1e-12 (the integrand is bounded, smooth on (0, ПҖ) for any non-critical h, and has a finite limit at the endpoints).

QAtlas._tfim_sigma_x_quench_obc вҖ” Method
_tfim_sigma_x_quench_obc(N, J, h_0, h_f, i, t) -> Float64

Exact вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©(t) for the OBC TFIM after a sudden quench h_0 вҶ’ h_f at fixed J, computed from the Majorana covariance of the initial ground state propagated by the post-quench Hamiltonian:

ОЈ_0   = _majorana_covariance_gs(_majorana_ham(N, J, h_0))
R(t)  = _majorana_evolution(_majorana_ham(N, J, h_f), t)
ОЈ(t)  = R(t) ОЈ_0 R(t)^T
вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©(t) = ОЈ(t)[2i-1, 2i]   (real).

A single (i, t) point costs one 2N Г— 2N eigendecomposition for ОЈ0 plus one matrix exponential for R(t). Sweeps in i should reuse the returned matrix; sweeps in t should be hoisted to a custom loop that caches `ОЈ0and recomputes onlyR(t)`.

_tfim_transverse_obc(quantity, N, J, h, ОІ) -> Float64

Compute m_x or ПҮ_xx per site for OBC finite N by direct site-resolved BdG expectation. Uses the Majorana covariance formula

ОЈ(ОІ) = -i tanh(ОІ/2 В· i h_BdG)

(see TFIM_dynamics.jl) and identifies вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ© = ОЈ[2i-1, 2i].

source
QAtlas._tfim_zz_structure_factor_dynamic_proxy вҖ” Method
_tfim_zz_structure_factor_dynamic_proxy(J, h, ОІ, q, Пү, N_proxy, t_max, dt) -> Float64

OBC large-N proxy implementation of the dynamic longitudinal structure factor S_zz(q, Пү; ОІ). Used by the Infinite() fetch router; the heavy lifting is performed here so the public method stays a thin wrapper.

The Fourier integral is replaced by a finite Riemann sum on t вҲҲ [-t_max, t_max] with spacing dt, and i, j run over the central bulk window [N/4, 3N/4] of an N_proxy-site OBC chain to suppress boundary contamination. The Majorana Hamiltonian and thermal covariance are computed once; the evolution matrix R(t) is recomputed at every time step (single 2N Г— 2N expm).

QAtlas._xx_uniform_susceptibility вҖ” Method
_xx_uniform_susceptibility(N, J, h, ОІ) -> Float64

Exact transverse susceptibility per site for the OBC TFIM,

ПҮ_xx(ОІ) = (ОІ/N) Var(ОЈбөў ПғЛЈбөў)
        = (ОІ/N) ОЈбөўвұј [ вҹЁПғЛЈбөў ПғЛЈвұјвҹ©_ОІ вҲ’ вҹЁПғЛЈбөўвҹ©_ОІ вҹЁПғЛЈвұјвҹ©_ОІ ]

Uses the Majorana covariance matrix ОЈ[a,b] = вҹЁОівӮҗОібөҰвҹ© вҲ’ ОҙвӮҗбөҰ. With ПғЛЈбөў = -i Оі_{2i-1} Оі_{2i} the connected correlators follow from Wick's theorem:

Diagonal (i = j): вҹЁ(ПғЛЈбөў)ВІвҹ©c = 1 вҲ’ ОЈ[2i-1, 2i]ВІ Off-diagonal (i вү  j): вҹЁПғЛЈбөў ПғЛЈвұјвҹ©c = вҲ’ОЈ[2i-1,2j-1]В·ОЈ[2i,2j] + ОЈ[2i-1,2j]В·ОЈ[2i,2j-1]

No numerical differentiation; no Pfaffian library calls.
