QAtlas._xxz1d_energy_yang_yang вҖ” Method
_xxz1d_energy_yang_yang(J, О”; rtol = 1e-12, atol = 1e-14) -> Float64

Ground-state energy per site of the spin-ВҪ XXZ chain in the thermodynamic limit, evaluated by the YangвҖ“Yang single-integral formula

eвӮҖ(О”) = (J cos Оі)/4 вҲ’ J sinВІ Оі В· вҲ«_{-вҲһ}^{вҲһ} dО» /
        [2 cosh(ПҖО») В· (cosh(2ОіО») вҲ’ cos Оі)],

with О” = cos Оі, Оі вҲҲ (0, ПҖ) (critical / gapless regime). The three canonical points О” вҲҲ {-1, 0, 1} are dispatched in the caller for exactness; this helper is invoked only for general -1 < О” < 1 with О” вҲү {0}. Tolerance defaults give relative error вүӨ 1e-12 against the closed-form values at О” = 0, Вұ1 (verified in test_XXZ1D.jl).

Cost: a few QuadGK panel splits, вүҲ 50 Вөs per call on a recent CPU.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::AKLT2D, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite; J=m.J) -> Float64

Ground-state energy density of the 2D AKLT model on the honeycomb lattice (Affleck-Kennedy-Lieb-Tasaki 1988):

e_0 / N = 0

The Hamiltonian is a sum of non-negative spin-3 projectors, and the valence-bond-solid (VBS) state is annihilated by every term вҶ’ frustration-free with exact zero ground-state energy density. The VBS state is the prototypical 2D AKLT-class SPT and a paradigmatic non-trivial PEPS (bond dimension 2).

References

  • I. Affleck, T. Kennedy, E. H. Lieb, H. Tasaki, Commun. Math. Phys. 115, 477 (1988).
  • F. Verstraete, J. I. Cirac, cond-mat/0407066 (2004) вҖ” PEPS realisation.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::BCFT, ::ResidualEntropy, ::Infinite; state::Symbol=:fixed) -> Float64

Return the Affleck-Ludwig boundary entropy log g_a for an Ising-CFT Cardy boundary state a.

stateglog g
:fixed, :fixed_plus, :fixed_minus1/вҲҡ2-log(2)/2
:identity, :vacuum1/вҲҡ2-log(2)/2
:epsilon, :energy1/вҲҡ2-log(2)/2
:free, :sigma10

The :free and :sigma symbols are synonyms: the physical free-spin boundary of the critical Ising model coincides with the |Пғвҹ© Cardy state, whose g-factor is g_Пғ = S_{Пғ,1}/вҲҡS_{1,1} = 1. The fixed-spin boundaries |Вұвҹ© вҲқ |1вҹ© Вұ |Оөвҹ© each have g = 1/вҲҡ2, as do the bare primary Cardy states |1вҹ© and |Оөвҹ©.

Throws a DomainError for any other state symbol (Phase 1 only supports Ising Cardy boundary states; other CFTs are Phase 2).

fetch(::ChernSimons3D, ::PartitionFunction, ::Infinite; N=m.N, k=m.k) -> Float64

Closed-form partition function of 3-D SU(N)_k Chern-Simons on the three-sphere SВі (Witten 1989), equal to the S_{0,0} entry of the SU(N)_k modular S-matrix (Verlinde formula):

Z(SВі; SU(N)_k) = N^{-1/2} (k + N)^{-(N-1)/2}
                 вҲҸ_{1 вүӨ j < l вүӨ N} 2 sin( ПҖ (l вҲ’ j) / (k + N) ).

For SU(2)_k this simplifies to Z = вҲҡ(2 / (k + 2)) В· sin(ПҖ / (k + 2)).

Boundary condition

Infinite() вҖ” SВі is a closed compact 3-manifold without boundary; no transfer-matrix BC label is meaningful, so the BC slot is the catch-all Infinite tag also used for thermodynamic-limit quantities elsewhere in QAtlas.

Verified values

  • SU(2)_1: Z = 1/вҲҡ2 вүҲ 0.7071067811865476
  • SU(2)_2: Z = 1/2 = 0.5
  • SU(2)_3: Z = вҲҡ(2/5) В· sin(ПҖ/5) вүҲ 0.3717480344601845
  • SU(3)_1: Z = 1/вҲҡ3 вүҲ 0.5773502691896258

References

  • E. Witten, Comm. Math. Phys. 121, 351 (1989).
  • E. P. Verlinde, Nucl. Phys. B 300, 360 (1988).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::CurieWeissIsing, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, J=m.J, h=m.h) -> Float64

Internal energy per site

u(ОІ, J, h) = -J m*ВІ / 2 - h m*.

At J вүӨ 0: single-spin, u = -h tanh(ОІh). At J > 0, h = 0, T > T_c: u = 0 (paramagnet). At J > 0, T вҶ’ 0, h вүҘ 0: u вҶ’ -J/2 - h (saturated).

References

  • L. D. Landau, E. M. Lifshitz, Statistical Physics В§149.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::CurieWeissIsing, ::FreeEnergy, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, J=m.J, h=m.h) -> Float64

Saddle-point free energy per site

f(ОІ, J, h) = J m*ВІ/2 - ОІвҒ»В№ log[2 cosh(ОІ(J m* + h))],

with m*(ОІ, J, h) the unique stable SCE root. Limits:

  • J вүӨ 0: non-interacting single spin in field, f = -ОІвҒ»В№ log(2 cosh(ОІh)).
  • J > 0, h = 0, T > T_c: paramagnet, f = -log(2)/ОІ.
  • J > 0, T вҶ’ 0: saturated, f вҶ’ -J/2 - |h|.

References

  • L. D. Landau, E. M. Lifshitz, Statistical Physics В§149.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::CurieWeissIsing, ::SpecificHeat, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, J=m.J, h=m.h) -> Float64

Specific heat per site

c_v(ОІ, J, h) = ОІВІ (J m* + h)ВІ (1 - m*ВІ) / (1 - ОІ J (1 - m*ВІ)).

Derived from u(ОІ) = -J m*ВІ/2 - h m* and dm*/dОІ via implicit differentiation of the SCE. At J > 0, h = 0: zero for T > T_c, jumps to 3/2 at T_cвҒ» (mean-field Landau jump). At J вүӨ 0: non-interacting, c_v = (ОІh)ВІ sechВІ(ОІh).

References

  • L. D. Landau, E. M. Lifshitz, Statistical Physics В§149.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::CurieWeissIsing, ::SpontaneousMagnetization, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, J=m.J) -> Float64

Spontaneous magnetisation m*(ОІ) = lim_{h вҶ’ 0вҒә} m(ОІ, J, h) of the Curie-Weiss Ising model: the в„ӨвӮӮ-positive nontrivial root of m = tanh(ОІJm).

By definition this dispatch always uses the zero-field SCE branch (the model's h field is ignored), since "spontaneous" magnetisation is the symmetry-broken value that survives in the field-free limit. For T вүҘ T_c = J only the trivial m = 0 root exists and 0.0 is returned; otherwise bisection on g(m) = m - tanh(ОІJm) over [m_min, 1) converges in ~52 steps (no rate degeneracy at criticality).

References

  • L. D. Landau, E. M. Lifshitz, Statistical Physics В§149.

Longitudinal isothermal susceptibility per site

ПҮ(ОІ, J, h) = ОІ (1 - m*ВІ) / (1 - ОІ J (1 - m*ВІ)).

Derived by implicit differentiation of m* = tanh(ОІ(Jm* + h)) w.r.t. h. Reduces to the Curie-Weiss law ПҮ = ОІ / (1 - ОІJ) above T_c (where m* = 0). Diverges at T_cвҒ» from the m* = 0 side. At J вүӨ 0: non-interacting, ПҮ = ОІ sechВІ(ОІh).

s(ОІ, J, h) = log[2 cosh(ОІ(J m* + h))]  -  ОІ(J m* + h) m*.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::DMIHeisenberg1D, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite;
      J=m.J, D=m.D) -> Float64

Ground-state energy density of the spin-ВҪ Heisenberg-DM chain in the thermodynamic limit. Phase 1 supports only the closed-form D = 0 point:

  • D = 0 вҶ’ Bethe-HulthГ©n: E/N = J В· (1/4 вҲ’ ln 2). Delegates to fetch(Heisenberg1D(), GroundStateEnergyDensity(), Infinite(); J=J).

  • D вү  0 вҶ’ DomainError: spiral order via gauge rotation to twisted XXZ (Affleck-Oshikawa 1999); closed-form Bethe-ansatz energy technically available but deferred to Phase 2.

Floating-point tolerance for the D = 0 match is atol = 1e-12.

Note on delegation: Heisenberg1D currently exposes its thermodynamic- limit energy density via the legacy GroundStateEnergyDensity quantity, not the modern Energy{:per_site} axis. This wrapper bridges to the modern axis on the public surface while keeping the closed-form constant single-source-of-truth in the Heisenberg1D delegate.

  • T. Moriya, Phys. Rev. 120, 91 (1960).

Оі = log рқ’ҹ = (1/2) log(2 + ПҶ)  вүҲ  0.6429653906

where рқ’ҹ = вҲҡ(d1ВІ + dП„ВІ) = вҲҡ(1 + ПҶВІ) = вҲҡ(ПҶ + 2) is the total quantum dimension and ПҶ = (1 + вҲҡ5)/2 is the golden ratio (= d_П„, the quantum dimension of the non-trivial П„ anyon).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::GrossNeveu, ::CentralCharge, ::Infinite; N=m.N, g=m.g) -> Int

Free-fermion UV central charge of the Gross-Neveu model:

c(g = 0) = N

(N Dirac fermions in 1+1-D, each c = 1). At any g вү  0 the theory is massive in the IR (dynamical chiral symmetry breaking; Gross-Neveu 1974) and the IR central charge is zero; this Phase 1 exposes only the UV g = 0 value and raises DomainError for non-zero coupling, deferring the RG-flow case to Phase 2.

  • D. J. Gross, A. Neveu, Phys. Rev. D 10, 3235 (1974).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::GrossNeveu, ::MassGap, ::Infinite; Оӣ::Real, N=m.N, g=m.g) -> Float64

Dynamically generated fermion mass m_F in the large-N Gross-Neveu model (Gross-Neveu 1974):

m_F = Оӣ В· exp(вҲ’ПҖ / (N В· gВІ)).

Оӣ is the renormalisation scheme's UV cutoff / dimensional-transmutation scale and is a required keyword argument вҖ” it is intentionally not stored on the GrossNeveu struct because the choice of scheme is up to the caller. The exponential suppression at weak coupling is the textbook signature of asymptotic-freedom-driven mass-gap formation.

Оӣ > 0, g > 0, N вүҘ 1 required (DomainError otherwise).

Examples

  • fetch(GrossNeveu(; N=1, g=1.0), MassGap(), Infinite(); Оӣ=1.0) вҶ’ exp(-ПҖ) вүҲ 0.0432139
  • fetch(GrossNeveu(; N=2, g=1.0), MassGap(), Infinite(); Оӣ=1.0) вҶ’ exp(-ПҖ/2) вүҲ 0.2078796

References

  • D. J. Gross, A. Neveu, Phys. Rev. D 10, 3235 (1974).
  • N. Andrei, J. H. Lowenstein, Phys. Rev. Lett. 43, 1698 (1979).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Heisenberg1D, ::ExactSpectrum; N, J=1.0) -> Vector{Float64}

Return the sorted exact spectrum of the spin-1/2 Heisenberg Hamiltonian on an N-site chain or ring with boundary condition bc.

Supported cases

  • N=2, bc=:OBC (dimer): [-3J/4, J/4, J/4, J/4] (singlet Es = -3J/4, triplet Et = J/4, three-fold degenerate).
  • N=4, bc=:PBC (4-site ring): [-2J, -JГ—3, 0Г—7, +JГ—5] Ground state EвӮҖ = -2J (unique singlet). The ferromagnetic quintet sits at E = +J. The full degeneracy structure is: 1 singlet + 1 triplet + (1 singlet + 2 triplets at E=0) + 1 quintet.

Arguments

  • N::Int: number of spin-1/2 sites
  • J::Real: Heisenberg coupling constant (default 1.0; J > 0 AFM)
  • bc::Symbol: boundary condition, :OBC (default) or :PBC

References

A. Auerbach, "Interacting Electrons and Quantum Magnetism" (1994), В§2.
H. Bethe, Z. Physik 71, 205 (1931).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Heisenberg1D, ::GroundStateEnergyDensity, ::Infinite; J=1.0) -> Float64

BC-explicit dispatch sister of the legacy fetch(::Heisenberg1D, ::GroundStateEnergyDensity; J=1.0) method. The thermodynamic-limit ground-state energy density is only meaningful at Infinite, so the two methods return the same HulthГ©n value eвӮҖ = J(1/4 - ln 2). Provided so which(fetch, ::Heisenberg1D, ::GroundStateEnergyDensity, ::Infinite) resolves and the registry drift guard passes.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Heisenberg1D, ::GroundStateEnergyDensity; J=1.0) -> Float64

Exact ground-state energy per site of the spin-1/2 antiferromagnetic Heisenberg chain in the thermodynamic limit (N вҶ’ вҲһ, PBC):

eвӮҖ = J (1/4 вҲ’ ln 2) вүҲ вҲ’0.4431 J

This is one of the earliest and most celebrated results of the Bethe ansatz. The derivation proceeds by solving the Bethe equations for the ground state of

H = J ОЈбөў Sбөў В· SбөўвӮҠвӮҒ

in the limit N вҶ’ вҲһ, yielding a linear integral equation for the rapidity distribution whose solution gives the energy via integration.

Finite-size corrections

For a PBC chain of N sites, the ground-state energy density approaches eвӮҖ with corrections of order 1/NВІ (logarithmic corrections also present):

EвӮҖ(N)/N = eвӮҖ + O(1/NВІ)

See test/verification/test_universality_cross_check.jl for a finite-size extrapolation verification using ED at N = 4, 6, 8.

Arguments

  • J::Real: Heisenberg coupling constant (default 1.0; J > 0 AFM)

References

H. Bethe, "Zur Theorie der Metalle. I. Eigenwerte und Eigenfunktionen
  der linearen Atomkette", Z. Physik 71, 205вҖ“226 (1931) вҖ” original
  Bethe ansatz solution.
L. HulthГ©n, "Гңber das Austauschproblem eines Kristalles",
  Ark. Mat. Astron. Fys. 26A, No. 11, 1вҖ“106 (1938) вҖ” first
  evaluation of eвӮҖ = 1/4 вҲ’ ln 2 from the Bethe equations.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Heisenberg1D, ::ZZStructureFactor, ::Infinite;
      q::Real, Пү::Real, method::Symbol = :muller, J::Real = 1.0,
      kwargs...) -> Float64

Longitudinal dynamic structure factor S^{zz}(q, Пү) of the infinite-volume spin-ВҪ XXX antiferromagnetic Heisenberg chain in the thermodynamic limit.

The default method = :muller evaluates the MГјller-ansatz closed form inside the two-spinon continuum (see _heisenberg_szz_muller):

S^{zz}(q, Пү) вүҲ  Оҳ[Пү вҲ’ Оө_L(q)] В· Оҳ[Оө_U(q) вҲ’ Пү]
                ----------------------------------
                    2 вҲҡ(ПүВІ вҲ’ Оө_L(q)ВІ)

with edges defined by heisenberg_two_spinon_lower_edge and heisenberg_two_spinon_upper_edge. Outside the continuum the routine returns 0.0. No regulator is added at the lower edge: the singularity is integrable (вҲқ 1/вҲҡ(Пү вҲ’ ОөL) for Пү вҶ’ ОөLвҒә), and any quadrature scheme used downstream should treat it analytically rather than relying on a numerical cap.

Arguments

  • q::Real: total momentum (radians).
  • Пү::Real: frequency (energy units consistent with J).
  • method::Symbol = :muller: ansatz selector; only :muller is implemented in Phase 1. Reserved future values: :caux_hagemans for the exact form-factor sum (Phase 2).
  • J::Real = 1.0: Heisenberg coupling.

References

G. MГјller, H. Thomas, H. Beck, J. C. Bonner, "Quantum spin
  dynamics of the antiferromagnetic linear chain in zero and
  nonzero magnetic field", Phys. Rev. B 24, 1429 (1981).
J.-S. Caux, R. Hagemans, "The four-spinon dynamical structure
  factor of the Heisenberg chain", J. Stat. Mech. P12013 (2006)
  (Phase 2 reference, not yet implemented).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::HeisenbergXYZ, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite;
      Jx=m.Jx, Jy=m.Jy, Jz=m.Jz, kwargs...) -> Float64

Ground-state energy per site of the spin-ВҪ XYZ chain in the thermodynamic limit, restricted to the axis-aligned reduction Jx = Jy:

HeisenbergXYZ(Jx = J, Jy = J, Jz)   вҹ¶   fetch(XXZ1D(J = J, О” = Jz/J), вҖҰ).

This routes the call through the XXZ1D Yang-Yang single integral (general -1 < О” < 1) and the three closed-form points О” вҲҲ {-1, 0, 1} already implemented in XXZ1D. General (Jx вү  Jy) triples require the Baxter elliptic Bethe ansatz and currently raise DomainError вҖ” Phase 2.

Jx > 0 is required (so Delta = Jz/Jx is well-defined and the delegation routes into the XXZ1D-tested domain; FM-exchange Jx < 0 is Phase 2).

References

  • C. N. Yang, C. P. Yang, Phys. Rev. 150, 327 (1966).
  • R. J. Baxter, Annals Phys. 70, 193 (1972).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::HeisenbergXYZ, ::LuttingerParameter, ::Infinite;

Luttinger-liquid parameter at the isotropic Heisenberg point Jx = Jy = Jz, delegated to XXZ1D(О” = 1):

K = 1/2          (SU(2)-symmetric AFM, Luther-Peschel 1975)

The delegation chain is HeisenbergXYZ вҶ’ XXZ1D(О”=1) (matching the Energy(:per_site) reduction). Once a dedicated fetch(::Heisenberg1D, ::LuttingerParameter, ::Infinite) lands on main (tracked separately), the intermediate Heisenberg1D hop can be reinstated; the final K is unchanged.

For Jx = Jy вү  Jz (XXZ axial anisotropy), use XXZ1D directly. For generic XYZ (Baxter 1972 elliptic / theta-function regime), defer to a later phase вҖ” this Phase-2 path throws DomainError for non-isotropic couplings.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Hubbard1D, ::ChargeGap, ::Infinite) -> Float64

LiebвҖ“Wu Mott (charge) gap at half filling:

О”_c = (16 tВІ / U) вҲ«_1^вҲһ dПү  вҲҡ(ПүВІ - 1) / sinh(2ПҖ t Пү / U).

Strictly positive for any U > 0 (no Mott transition in 1D вҖ” the chain is insulating at half filling for arbitrarily small U, the celebrated LiebвҖ“Wu result).

Asymptotic limits

  • U вҶ’ 0: О”_c вҶ’ 0 (exponentially small, вҲқ exp(-2ПҖ t / U)).
  • U вҶ’ вҲһ: О”_c вҶ’ U - 4t + 8 tВІ log 2 / U.

References

  • LiebвҖ“Wu, PRL 20, 1445 (1968).

fetch(::IsingChain1D, ::CorrelationLength, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, J=m.J, h=m.h) -> Float64

Spin-spin correlation length Оҫ(ОІ, h) = 1 / log(О»_+ / О»_-) of the 1-D Ising chain, with О»_Вұ the two transfer-matrix eigenvalues. At h = 0 this reduces to the Ising 1925 form

Оҫ(ОІ, 0) = 1 / log(coth(ОІ J)).

The correlation length is finite for every T > 0 (no finite-temperature phase transition) and diverges only in the zero-temperature ferromagnetic limit T вҶ’ 0вҒә at J > 0.

References

  • E. Ising, Z. Phys. 31, 253 (1925).
source

Critical temperature of the 1-D Ising chain. Ising (1925) proved that no finite-temperature phase transition occurs in 1-D; the only singular point is T = 0. Returns 0.0.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::IsingSquare, ::CriticalExponents, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> NamedTuple

Onsager 1944 critical exponents of the 2D square-lattice Ising model at T_c (= 2J / log(1 + вҲҡ2)):

Оұ = 0,  ОІ = 1/8,  Оі = 7/4,  Оҙ = 15,  ОҪ = 1,  О· = 1/4.

Delegated to the existing Universality(:Ising) infrastructure at d = 2. Rushbrooke (Оұ + 2ОІ + Оі = 2), Widom (Оі = ОІ(Оҙ вҲ’ 1)), and Fisher (О· = 2 вҲ’ Оі/ОҪ) hyperscaling relations all check out.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::IsingSquare, ::PartitionFunction; Lx, Ly, ОІ, J=1.0) -> Real

Exact partition function Z = Tr(T^Lx) for the classical 2D Ising model on an Lx Г— Ly square lattice with periodic boundary conditions in both directions.

The transfer matrix T acts along the Lx direction (row-to-row transfer), with each row containing Ly spins and PBC along the Ly direction.

Bond-counting convention

The transfer-matrix sum double-counts bonds along any dimension of length 2 (PBC wraparound of a length-2 ring produces the factor Пғ_1 Пғ_2 + Пғ_2 Пғ_1 = 2 Пғ_1 Пғ_2). The brute-force enumeration in test/util/classical_partition.jl is built under the same PBC convention so that Z_transfer-matrix == Z_bruteforce exactly for every (Lx, Ly, ОІ, J). For Lx вүҘ 3 and Ly вүҘ 3 each physical bond is enumerated exactly once and the result coincides with the standard physical Z of a PBC lattice.

Special values

  • ОІ = 0 (any Lx, Ly, J): Z = 2^(LxВ·Ly) вҖ” all configurations equally weighted
  • J = 0 (any ОІ, Lx, Ly): Z = 2^(LxВ·Ly) вҖ” no interactions, same as ОІ = 0

Automatic differentiation

fetch is generic in ОІ and J so that ForwardDiff.Dual numbers propagate through it. This allows macroscopic thermodynamic quantities to be recovered from Z by differentiation вҖ” e.g.

вҹЁEвҹ© = -вҲӮ(log Z)/вҲӮОІ
C_v = ОІВІ В· вҲӮВІ(log Z)/вҲӮОІВІ

See test/verification/test_ising_ad_thermodynamics.jl for a cross-check against direct ensemble averages.

Arguments

  • Lx::Int: number of rows (transfer direction)
  • Ly::Int: number of columns (row length, PBC)
  • ОІ::Real: inverse temperature (ОІ = 1/(k_B T))
  • J::Real: Ising coupling constant (default 1.0; J > 0 ferromagnetic)

References

L. Onsager, Phys. Rev. 65, 117 (1944).
B. M. McCoy and T. T. Wu, "The Two-Dimensional Ising Model" (1973).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::IsingSquare, ::SpecificHeat, ::Infinite; beta, J=m.J) -> Float64

Per-site specific heat c_v(ОІ) = ОІВІ В· вҲӮВІ(log Z / N)/вҲӮОІВІ via ForwardDiff (twice). Diverges logarithmically at the Onsager critical point K_c = ln(1+вҲҡ2)/2 (i.e. T_c = 2J/ln(1+вҲҡ2)). Caller is responsible for staying off that slice; finite values everywhere else.

source

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::IsingSquare, ::SpontaneousMagnetization; ОІ, J=1.0) -> Float64

Exact spontaneous magnetization of the 2D Ising model on the infinite square lattice:

M(T) = (1 вҲ’ sinhвҒ»вҒҙ(2ОІJ))^{1/8}    for T < T_c  (i.e. sinh(2ОІJ) > 1)
M(T) = 0                            for T вүҘ T_c

The critical exponent ОІ = 1/8 is visible in the approach M вҶ’ 0 as T вҶ’ T_cвҒ».

Special values:

  • T = T_c: M = 0 (onset of disorder)

Arguments

  • J::Real: Ising coupling constant (default 1.0; J > 0 ferromagnetic)

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::IsingTriangular, ::CriticalExponents, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> NamedTuple

2D Ising universality critical exponents (Onsager 1944), shared by the square and triangular lattices via universality:

Оұ = 0,  ОІ = 1/8,  Оі = 7/4,  Оҙ = 15,  ОҪ = 1,  О· = 1/4.

Delegated to Universality(:Ising) at d = 2. The triangular and square 2D Ising lattices have different microscopic T_c (Onsager's $2/log(1+sqrt(2))$ for the square; Houtappel's $4/log 3$ for the FM triangular) but identical universal exponents вҖ” the canonical textbook example of universality.

References

  • L. Onsager, Phys. Rev. 65, 117 (1944).
  • R. M. F. Houtappel, Physica 16, 425 (1950) вҖ” exact triangular-lattice Ising solution.
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::IsingTriangular, ::CriticalTemperature, ::Infinite; J=m.J) -> Float64

Exact critical temperature of the classical 2D Ising model on the triangular lattice in the Wannier 1950 sign convention $H = +J ОЈ Пғ_i Пғ_j$:

  • J > 0 (AFM, frustrated) вҖ” T_c = 0. No long-range order at any positive temperature (Wannier 1950).
  • J < 0 (FM, Houtappel) вҖ” T_c = 4 |J| / ln 3 вүҲ 3.6409 |J| (Houtappel 1950).
  • J = 0 вҖ” T_c = 0 (no interaction; degenerate value, kept finite).

References

  • G. H. Wannier, Phys. Rev. 79, 357 (1950).
  • R. M. F. Houtappel, Physica 16, 425 (1950).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::IsingTriangular, ::ResidualEntropy, ::Infinite; J=m.J) -> Float64

Zero-temperature residual entropy per site of the classical Ising model on the triangular lattice in the Wannier 1950 sign convention $H = +J ОЈ Пғ_i Пғ_j$.

  • J > 0 (frustrated AFM) вҖ” Wannier (1950) closed form

    S/(N k_B) = (2/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^{ПҖ/3} ln(2 cos Оё) dОё вүҲ 0.32306594722вҖҰ

    The integral is evaluated by QuadGK.quadgk to ~1e-12 precision.

  • J вүӨ 0 (FM or non-interacting Ising on a triangular lattice) вҖ” there is a unique pair of degenerate FM ground states related by the global в„ӨвӮӮ flip, so S_residual = 0.

References

  • G. H. Wannier, "Antiferromagnetism. The triangular Ising net", Phys. Rev. 79, 357 (1950).
  • R. M. F. Houtappel, Physica 16, 425 (1950) вҖ” independent derivation in the same period.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::J1J2Heisenberg1D, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite;
      J1=m.J1, J2=m.J2) -> Float64

Ground-state energy density of the spin-ВҪ JвӮҒ-JвӮӮ Heisenberg chain in the thermodynamic limit. Phase 1 supports only the two closed-form points:

  • j = JвӮӮ/JвӮҒ = 0 вҶ’ Bethe-HulthГ©n: E/N = JвӮҒ В· (1/4 вҲ’ ln 2). Delegates to fetch(Heisenberg1D(), GroundStateEnergyDensity(), Infinite(); J=J1).

  • j = 1/2 вҶ’ Majumdar-Ghosh dimer GS: E/N = вҲ’3 JвӮҒ / 8. Delegates to fetch(MajumdarGhosh(; J=J1), GroundStateEnergyDensity(), Infinite()).

  • otherwise вҶ’ DomainError: no closed form; numerical DMRG required, deferred to Phase 2.

Floating-point tolerance for the j = 0 and j = 1/2 matches is atol = 1e-12.

Note on delegation: Heisenberg1D and MajumdarGhosh currently expose their thermodynamic-limit energy density via the legacy GroundStateEnergyDensity quantity, not the modern Energy{:per_site} axis. This wrapper bridges to the modern axis on the public surface while keeping the closed-form constants in a single source-of-truth location (the delegate model).

References

  • L. HulthГ©n, Ark. Mat. Astron. Fys. 26A, No. 11 (1938) вҖ” Bethe-HulthГ©n ground-state energy density.
  • C. K. Majumdar, D. K. Ghosh, J. Math. Phys. 10, 1388 (1969) вҖ” exact dimer ground state at j = 1/2.
  • S. R. White, I. Affleck, Phys. Rev. B 54, 9862 (1996) вҖ” DMRG study of generic j (deferred to Phase 2).

e_0 / J вүҲ -0.4386(5)

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::KagomeHeisenbergAFM, ::MassGap, ::Infinite; J=m.J) -> Float64

Spin gap of the spin-ВҪ Kagome AFM:

О”_s / J вүҲ 0.13

(Yan-Huse-White 2011 DMRG; gapped ZвӮӮ spin liquid scenario). Returned as J Г— 0.13. Variational Monte Carlo (Iqbal-Becca- Sorella-Poilblanc 2013) favours a competing gapless U(1) Dirac spin liquid, so the spin gap value should be treated as a DMRG upper bound; reliability is therefore :medium.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::KagomeHeisenbergAFM, ::TopologicalEntanglementEntropy, ::Infinite; kwargs...)
    -> Float64

Topological entanglement entropy Оі = log 2 for the ZвӮӮ spin-liquid ground-state scenario. In the Kitaev-Preskill (2006) / Levin-Wen (2006) prescription,

S(ПҒ_A) = Оұ |вҲӮA| вҲ’ Оі + O(|вҲӮA|вҒ»В№),

with Оі = log рқ’ҹ and total quantum dimension рқ’ҹ = вҲҡ(ОЈ_a d_aВІ) = 2 for ZвӮӮ topological order (four Abelian anyons {1, e, m, ПҲ}, each with d_a = 1).

Reliability is :medium вҖ” the value is the ZвӮӮ topological prediction (Yan-Huse-White 2011 DMRG; Jiang-Wang-Balents 2012 directly extracted Оі вүҲ log 2 from DMRG entanglement scans), but the competing U(1) Dirac-spin-liquid scenario (Iqbal-Becca-Sorella-Poilblanc 2013) gives a gapless variational ground state with no topological order; the precise spin-liquid character is an open question.

References

  • A. Kitaev, J. Preskill, Phys. Rev. Lett. 96, 110404 (2006).
  • M. Levin, X.-G. Wen, Phys. Rev. Lett. 96, 110405 (2006).
  • H.-C. Jiang, Z. Wang, L. Balents, Nature Phys. 8, 902 (2012).
  • S. Yan, D. A. Huse, S. R. White, Science 332, 1173 (2011).

\[\xi = \frac{1}{\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}}}.\]

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Kitaev1D, ::EdgeModeEnergy, bc::OBC; N::Int) -> Float64

Energy of the lowest-lying boundary mode on an N-site OBC Kitaev1D chain вҖ” the smallest non-negative BdG eigenvalue.

In the topological phase (|Ој| < 2|t|, О” вү  0) the two end-localised Majorana modes hybridise into a single complex fermion with exponentially-small splitting ~ e^{-N/Оҫ} where Оҫ ~ 1/log(2|t|/|Ој|) for |Ој| вүӘ 2|t|.

Numerically equal to fetch(model, MassGap(), OBC(N)); the two methods exist as separate names so call sites can be explicit about which physical interpretation they have in mind.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Kitaev1D, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite) -> Float64

Ground-state energy per site of the infinite Kitaev1D chain at T = 0,

\[\varepsilon_0 = -\frac{1}{2\pi} \int_{-\pi}^{\pi} \frac{E(k)}{2}\, dk, \qquad E(k) = \sqrt{(2t\cos k + \mu)^2 + 4\Delta^2 \sin^2 k}.\]

(The factor 1/2 accounts for the BdG particle-hole doubling: only the negative-energy band is filled.)

Computed by adaptive Gauss-Kronrod quadrature.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Kitaev1D, ::ExactSpectrum, bc::OBC; N::Int) -> Vector{Float64}

Return the N non-negative BdG quasiparticle energies of the OBC Kitaev1D chain, sorted ascending.

N is read from bc.N (OBC(N) / OBC(; N)) or, as a legacy fallback, from the N keyword argument.

In the topological phase (|Ој| < 2|t|, О” вү  0) the lowest entry is the exponentially-small Majorana edge-mode hybridisation energy ~ e^{-N/Оҫ}. In the trivial phase the lowest entry approaches the bulk gap min(|2t + Ој|, |2t - Ој|).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Kitaev1D, ::MassGap, ::Infinite) -> Float64

Bulk single-quasiparticle gap of the infinite Kitaev1D chain,

\[\Delta_{\mathrm{gap}} = \min_k \sqrt{(2t\cos k + \mu)^2 + 4\Delta^2 \sin^2 k}.\]

Closed form (for t вү  0, О” вү  0):

  • |Ој| вүҘ 2|t|: minimum at k = 0 or k = ПҖ, giving О”_gap = ||Ој| - 2|t||.
  • |Ој| < 2|t|: stationary point at cos k* = -Ој t / (2(tВІ - О”ВІ)) when |t| вү  |О”| and |cos k*| вүӨ 1; otherwise the minimum is at k = 0 or k = ПҖ.

О” = 0 gives the gapless metal whenever |Ој| < 2|t|, and the routine returns 0.0 in that case.

MassGap at OBC is provided as the smallest non-negative BdG eigenvalue (numerically equal to EdgeModeEnergy at OBC).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Kitaev1D, ::MassGap, bc::OBC; N::Int) -> Float64

Single-quasiparticle gap of the N-site OBC Kitaev1D chain вҖ” the smallest non-negative BdG eigenvalue of the 2N Г— 2N BdG matrix.

In the topological phase this is the Majorana edge-mode energy ~ e^{-N/Оҫ} (use EdgeModeEnergy for the same value under a boundary-mode-explicit name). In the trivial phase it converges to the bulk gap as N вҶ’ вҲһ.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::Kitaev1D, ::TopologicalInvariant, ::Infinite) -> Int

Pfaffian ZвӮӮ invariant of the infinite Kitaev1D chain (Kitaev 2001),

\[\nu = \operatorname{sgn}\bigl[\operatorname{Pf} A(k=0) \cdot \operatorname{Pf} A(k=\pi)\bigr] = \operatorname{sgn}\bigl[(\mu + 2t)(\mu - 2t)\bigr] = \operatorname{sgn}(\mu^2 - 4t^2).\]

Returns -1 in the topological phase (|Ој| < 2|t|) and +1 in the trivial phase (|Ој| > 2|t|). Throws on the gapless line |Ој| = 2|t| (Pfaffian vanishes; invariant ill-defined) and on the gapless metal О” = 0 with |Ој| < 2|t|.

The two 2 Г— 2 Pfaffians are computed using the generic pfaffian routine in src/core/pfaffian.jl, exercising the same numerical machinery used elsewhere in QAtlas for free-fermion Wick contractions.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::KitaevHeisenberg, ::MassGap, ::Infinite;
      K=m.K, J=m.J, О“=m.О“, kwargs...) -> Float64

Single-particle gap of the K-J-О“ honeycomb model at the K-only point J = О“ = 0. Internally constructs the isotropic KitaevHoneycomb(Kx = K, Ky = K, Kz = K) and forwards. The Kitaev gapless A/B/C phase therefore returns О” = 0 at isotropic |K|.

J вү  0 or О“ вү  0 raises DomainError вҖ” Phase 2.

References

  • A. Kitaev, Annals Phys. 321, 2 (2006).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::KitaevHoneycomb, ::Energy{:per_site}, bc::PBC; Lx, Ly) -> Float64

Per-site ground state energy on a Lx Г— Ly unit-cell torus (PBC in both lattice directions) вҖ” enumerates all four topological flux sectors and returns the minimum. Each sector corresponds to a choice of fermion boundary conditions (W_x, W_y вҲҲ {Вұ1}); Lieb's theorem fixes plaquette fluxes at +1, so the spin-Hamiltonian ground state is one of these four.

Bond connectivity matches Lattice2D.build_lattice(Honeycomb, Lx, Ly; boundary=PeriodicAxis()). bc.N is ignored; pass Lx, Ly as kwargs.

For large L the four sectors converge to the same energy and individual Bloch-sum terms dominate; for small L sector choice is essential (e.g. Lx = Ly = 2 gives distinct sector energies differing by ~10%).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::KitaevHoneycomb, ::FreeEnergy, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, rtol=1e-8, kwargs...)

Per-site freeenergy of the infinite Kitaev honeycomb at inverse temperature beta, in the matter-sector free-fermion approximation (valid for `T вүӘ О”v`; see module header). Adaptive 2D Gauss-Kronrod quadrature over the BZ.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::KitaevHoneycomb, ::MassGap, ::Infinite) -> Float64

Single-Majorana gap in the thermodynamic limit.

О” = 2 В· min_k |f(k)|.

In the A/B/C gapless phase (each |Kбө§| вүӨ sum of the other two), f(k) has two linear (Dirac) zeros and О” = 0. In the gapped Az / Ax / Ay phases (|Kбө§| exceeds the sum of the other two), |f| is bounded away from zero and `О” = 2В·( |KОіmax| вҲ’ |KОіother1| вҲ’ |KОі_other2| )`.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::LiouvilleCFT, ::CentralCharge, ::Infinite; b=m.b) -> Float64

Central charge of Liouville CFT at coupling b > 0:

c = 1 + 6 (b + 1/b)ВІ.

b вҶ” 1/b self-duality leaves c invariant. Special points:

  • b = 1 вҶ’ Q = 2, c = 25 (self-dual point)
  • b вҶ’ 0вҒә вҶ’ Q вҶ’ вҲһ, c вҶ’ вҲһ (semi-classical / weak-coupling)
  • b вҶ’ вҲһ вҶ’ Q вҶ’ вҲһ, c вҶ’ вҲһ (strong-coupling dual)

b вүӨ 0 raises DomainError (the Liouville coupling is real and positive by convention; b вҶ” 1/b lives entirely on the positive half-line).

References

  • A. M. Polyakov, Phys. Lett. B 103, 207 (1981).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::LiouvilleCFT, ::ConformalWeights, ::Infinite; Оұ::Real, b=m.b) -> Float64

Conformal (scaling) dimension of the Liouville vertex operator V_Оұ(z, zМ„) = exp(2 Оұ ПҶ(z, zМ„)) at coupling b > 0 and continuous real momentum Оұ:

О”_Оұ = Оұ (Q вҲ’ Оұ),    Q = b + 1/b.

Both holomorphic and antiholomorphic weights coincide (h = hМ„ = О”_Оұ); the full scaling dimension of V_Оұ is 2 О”_Оұ.

О”_Оұ is invariant under the Liouville reflection Оұ вҶ” Q вҲ’ Оұ (the vertex operators V_Оұ and V_{QвҲ’Оұ} are identified up to the DOZZ reflection coefficient).

Special values:

  • Оұ = 0 вҶ’ О” = 0 (identity operator)
  • Оұ = Q/2 вҶ’ О” = QВІ/4 (boundary of the normalisable real-Оұ slice; "Seiberg bound")
  • Оұ = b вҶ’ О” = b(Q вҲ’ b) = 1 (degenerate screening operator V_b; conformal spin 1)
  • Оұ = 1/b вҶ’ О” = (1/b)(Q вҲ’ 1/b) = 1 (dual screening V_{1/b})
  • Оұ вҶ” QвҲ’Оұ вҶ’ О”_Оұ = О”_{QвҲ’Оұ} (reflection symmetry)

b вүӨ 0 raises DomainError (the Liouville coupling is real and positive by convention). Оұ is unconstrained: it may be any real number, including the non-normalisable region Оұ < 0 or Оұ > Q/2, where О”_Оұ still gives the formal scaling dimension.

References

  • A. M. Polyakov, Phys. Lett. B 103, 207 (1981).
  • A. B. Zamolodchikov, A. B. Zamolodchikov, Nucl. Phys. B 477, 577 (1996).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::LogarithmicCFT, ::CentralCharge, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> Rational{Int}

Central charge of the c = 0 logarithmic CFT (polymer / percolation universality):

c = 0.

Despite the vanishing central charge the theory is non-trivial вҖ” the dilatation operator L_0 admits indecomposable Jordan blocks, mixing pairs of primary fields under conformal transformations and producing logarithms in correlation functions (Pearce-Rasmussen-Zuber 2006; Vasseur-Jacobsen-Saleur 2011).

Phase 1 exposes only the central charge. Indecomposable representations and logarithmic operator content require new quantity types and are tracked as Phase 2.

References

  • H. Saleur, Nucl. Phys. B 382, 486 (1992).
  • J. Cardy, J. Phys. A 34, 1419 (2001).
  • P. A. Pearce, J. Rasmussen, J.-B. Zuber, J. Stat. Mech. P11017 (2006).
  • R. Vasseur, J. L. Jacobsen, H. Saleur, J. Stat. Mech. L07001 (2011).

Single-quasiparticle gap of the long-range TFIM at the Оұ = Inf nearest-neighbour limit. Internally constructs TFIM(; J=J, h=h) and forwards. Closed-form result (Pfeuty 1970):

О” = 2 |h - J|.

Finite Оұ raises DomainError вҖ” the long-range phase diagram (Koffel-Lewenstein-Tagliacozzo 2012, Gong-Foss-Feig 2014) requires numerical DMRG / VMC and is deferred to Phase 2.

EвӮҖ/N = вҲ’3J/8.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::MajumdarGhosh, ::GroundStateEnergyDensity, ::PBC; N::Int, kwargs...) -> Float64

Ground-state energy density for the MajumdarвҖ“Ghosh chain on a periodic ring of N sites. Because the dimer-product state is an exact eigenstate of the JвӮҒвҖ“JвӮӮ Hamiltonian at JвӮӮ/JвӮҒ = 1/2 for any even ring length, the per-site energy is вҲ’3J/8 independent of N.

N may be supplied either through PBC(N) or via the N kwarg; it must be a positive even integer (the dimer covering requires an even number of sites to close into a ring without a defect).

References

  • C. K. Majumdar, D. K. Ghosh, J. Math. Phys. 10, 1388 (1969).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::MajumdarGhosh, ::MassGap, ::Infinite; method::Symbol = :numerical) -> Float64

Spectral gap above the dimer ground state in the thermodynamic limit.

Two stored values are available, selected via method:

  • :numerical (default) вҖ” the DMRG value О” вүҲ 0.234 J (WhiteвҖ“ Affleck 1996; reproduced by Eggert 1996, Sandvik 2010). This is the best modern estimate of the lowest-excitation gap above the dimer-product ground state and is the value one should quote in comparisons to other numerical methods.

  • :trimer_bound вҖ” the analytical ShastryвҖ“Sutherland (1981) bound О”_trimer вүҘ J/4. The previous default; kept as a separately- labelled bound, not the gap. Note: the SS bound J/4 = 0.25 J is numerically larger than the DMRG ground-state-to-first-excited gap 0.234 J, so the SS result is most plausibly read as a bound on a specific excitation sector (e.g. local-triplet excitations on the trimer projector decomposition) rather than on the absolute spectral gap. Verified by my finite-N PBC dense ED at N = 8, 10, 12: gap monotone decreasing 0.405 вҶ’ 0.350 вҶ’ 0.319 J, already below J/4 at N = 12 and trending toward 0.234 J in the bulk limit.

    The legacy alias :lower_bound still resolves to this value for backward compatibility but emits a deprecation warning.

Any other symbol raises DomainError.

References

  • S. R. White, I. Affleck, Phys. Rev. B 54, 9862 (1996) вҖ” DMRG gap О” вүҲ 0.234 J (default).
  • S. Eggert, Phys. Rev. B 54, R9612 (1996) вҖ” independent DMRG confirmation.
  • B. S. Shastry, B. Sutherland, J. Phys. C 14, L765 (1981) вҖ” trimer lower bound О”_trimer вүҘ J/4 (sector-specific reading; see Caspers-Magnus 1982 / Magnus 1991 for refined rigorous bounds).
  • W. J. Caspers, W. Magnus, Physica A 111, 220 (1982) вҖ” rigorous bound О” вүҘ 0.0975 J on the absolute gap.
source

Ground-state-to-first-excited spin gap of the MajumdarвҖ“Ghosh chain:

О” вүҲ 0.234 J        (White-Affleck 1996; Eggert 1996 DMRG cross-check)

Returned as J Г— 0.234. Reliability :medium (numerical DMRG, finite extrapolation uncertainty; the value should be revised if a tighter literature consensus emerges). The analytical Shastry-Sutherland 1981 bound О” вүҘ J/4 = 0.25 J is larger than the DMRG value, so the SS bound is a sector-specific trimer-excitation bound, not the absolute gap.

  • S. Eggert, Phys. Rev. B 54, R9612 (1996).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::MinimalModel, ::ConformalWeights; r::Int, s::Int) -> Rational{Int}

Kac-table conformal weight of the primary (r, s):

h_{r,s} = ((p r - p_prime s)^2 - (p - p_prime)^2) / (4 p p_prime),
    1 вүӨ r вүӨ p_prime - 1,  1 вүӨ s вүӨ p - 1.

Out-of-range (r, s) throws DomainError. Use the Kac symmetry h_{r,s} = h_{p_prime - r, p - s} to map a label outside the fundamental rectangle into it explicitly.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::MinimalModel, ::PrimaryFields) -> Vector{NamedTuple}

All distinct primary fields of M(p, pprime), modulo Kac symmetry `(r, s) ~ (pprime - r, p - s). Each entry is a NamedTuple(r=Int, s=Int, h=Rational{Int})`.

The list is enumerated over 1 вүӨ r вүӨ p_prime - 1, 1 вүӨ s вүӨ p - 1 and de-duplicated by selecting the lex-smallest (r, s) from each Kac-symmetry orbit, so its length is

(p - 1)(p_prime - 1) / 2.

fetch(m::MixedFieldIsing1D, ::MassGap, ::Infinite; J, h_x, h_z) -> Float64

Mass gap of the infinite mixed-field Ising chain.

  • At h_z = 0 (default): delegate to TFIM(; J=J, h=h_x) and return the closed-form О” = 2|h_x вҲ’ J| (Pfeuty 1970).
  • At h_z вү  0: throw DomainError вҖ” the model is non-integrable (canonical ETH / thermalisation benchmark, McCoy-Wu 1978; Banuls-Cirac-Hastings 2011) and no closed-form gap exists. Numerical routes (ED / DMRG) will land in Phase 2.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Graphene, ::TightBindingSpectrum; Lx, Ly, t=1.0) -> Vector{Float64}

Sorted single-particle spectrum of the nearest-neighbor tight-binding Hamiltonian on an Lx Г— Ly honeycomb lattice with periodic boundary conditions in both directions.

The spectrum is obtained in closed form by diagonalizing the 2Г—2 Bloch Hamiltonian at the LxВ·Ly allowed momenta

k_{mn} = (m/Lx) bвӮҒ + (n/Ly) bвӮӮ,   m вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LxвҲ’1}, n вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LyвҲ’1}

where (bвӮҒ, bвӮӮ) is the reciprocal basis dual to the real-space basis (aвӮҒ, aвӮӮ) used by Lattice2D's Honeycomb topology.

Explicitly, using kВ·aвӮҒ = 2ПҖ m/Lx and kВ·aвӮӮ = 2ПҖ n/Ly,

E_{mn,Вұ} = Вұ t В· вҲҡ(3 + 2cos(2ПҖ m/Lx) + 2cos(2ПҖ n/Ly) + 2cos(2ПҖ(n/Ly вҲ’ m/Lx)))

The chiral (sublattice) symmetry of the bipartite honeycomb lattice guarantees that the spectrum is symmetric about zero. A small negative floor is applied inside the square root to absorb rounding error at Dirac points where the argument vanishes exactly.

Arguments

  • Lx::Int: number of unit cells in the first lattice direction
  • Ly::Int: number of unit cells in the second lattice direction
  • t::Real: nearest-neighbor hopping amplitude (default 1.0)

Return

A sorted Vector{Float64} of length 2В·LxВ·Ly.

References

P. R. Wallace, Phys. Rev. 71, 622 (1947).
A. H. Castro Neto et al., Rev. Mod. Phys. 81, 109 (2009).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Kagome, ::TightBindingChecksum, ::Infinite; Lx, Ly, t=1.0) -> Float64

ОЈ О»бөўВІ = tr(HВІ) for the Lx Г— Ly kagome PBC TB spectrum. Each unit cell has 3 sites with coordination 4 (two within-cell and two cross-cell nearest-neighbour bonds), giving n_NN_bonds = 6 В· Lx В· Ly and tr(HВІ) = 12 В· tВІ В· Lx В· Ly.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Kagome, ::TightBindingSpectrum; Lx, Ly, t=1.0) -> Vector{Float64}

Sorted single-particle spectrum of the nearest-neighbor tight-binding Hamiltonian on an Lx Г— Ly kagome lattice with periodic boundary conditions in both directions.

The 3Г—3 Bloch Hamiltonian is diagonalized numerically at each of the LxВ·Ly allowed momenta

k_{mn} = (m/Lx) bвӮҒ + (n/Ly) bвӮӮ,   m вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LxвҲ’1}, n вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LyвҲ’1}

with bвӮҒ, bвӮӮ dual to Lattice2D's kagome primitive basis. In the Оё parametrization (ОёвӮҒ = kВ·aвӮҒ = 2ПҖ m/Lx, ОёвӮӮ = kВ·aвӮӮ = 2ПҖ n/Ly),

H(k) = -2t В· [ 0              cos(ОёвӮҒ/2)           cos(ОёвӮӮ/2)        ]
             [ cos(ОёвӮҒ/2)      0                   cos((ОёвӮӮвҲ’ОёвӮҒ)/2)   ]
             [ cos(ОёвӮӮ/2)      cos((ОёвӮӮвҲ’ОёвӮҒ)/2)      0                ]

Flat band

One band is exactly flat at +2t, so the returned spectrum contains at least LxВ·Ly eigenvalues equal to 2t. At the О“-point (k = 0) the upper dispersive band touches the flat band, contributing one extra +2t eigenvalue, giving a LxВ·Ly + 1-fold degeneracy there. The remaining 2В·LxВ·Ly вҲ’ 1 eigenvalues lie in [вҲ’4t, +2t).

Arguments

  • Lx::Int: number of unit cells in the first lattice direction
  • Ly::Int: number of unit cells in the second lattice direction
  • t::Real: nearest-neighbor hopping amplitude (default 1.0)

Return

A sorted Vector{Float64} of length 3В·LxВ·Ly.

References

I. SyГҙzi, Prog. Theor. Phys. 6, 306 (1951).
D. L. Bergman et al., Phys. Rev. B 78, 125104 (2008).
source

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Lieb, ::TightBindingSpectrum; Lx, Ly, t=1.0) -> Vector{Float64}

Sorted single-particle spectrum of the nearest-neighbor tight-binding Hamiltonian on an Lx Г— Ly Lieb lattice with periodic boundary conditions in both directions.

The closed-form eigenvalues of the 3Г—3 Bloch Hamiltonian are

E_{mn,Вұ} = Вұ 2t В· вҲҡ(cosВІ(ПҖ m/Lx) + cosВІ(ПҖ n/Ly)),
E_{mn,0} = 0

for m вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LxвҲ’1}, n вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LyвҲ’1}. The E = 0 contribution appears for every (m, n) and forms the Lieb flat band.

Flat band

For a generic (Lx, Ly) the spectrum contains exactly LxВ·Ly zero eigenvalues from the flat band. When both Lx and Ly are even the M-point (ОёвӮҒ, ОёвӮӮ) = (ПҖ, ПҖ) becomes an allowed momentum; there the two dispersive bands also collapse to zero, contributing two extra zero modes (a three-fold band touching). The total number of E = 0 eigenvalues is therefore

LxВ·Ly + (2 if both Lx and Ly are even else 0).

Arguments

  • Lx::Int: number of unit cells in the first lattice direction
  • Ly::Int: number of unit cells in the second lattice direction
  • t::Real: nearest-neighbor hopping amplitude (default 1.0)

Return

A sorted Vector{Float64} of length 3В·LxВ·Ly.

References

E. H. Lieb, Phys. Rev. Lett. 62, 1201 (1989).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::Triangular, ::TightBindingSpectrum; Lx, Ly, t=1.0) -> Vector{Float64}

Sorted single-particle spectrum of the nearest-neighbor tight-binding Hamiltonian on an Lx Г— Ly triangular lattice with periodic boundary conditions in both directions.

Because the triangular lattice has a single sublattice per unit cell, each allowed momentum contributes exactly one eigenvalue

E_{mn} = -2t В· [ cos(2ПҖ m/Lx) + cos(2ПҖ n/Ly) + cos(2ПҖ(n/Ly вҲ’ m/Lx)) ]

for m вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LxвҲ’1}, n вҲҲ {0,вҖҰ,LyвҲ’1}. Note the lower cut-off is -6t (at the О“-point) but the upper cut-off is only +3t (at the K-points (1/3, 2/3) and (2/3, 1/3) вҖ” allowed when Lx and Ly are divisible by 3).

Arguments

  • Lx::Int: number of unit cells in the first lattice direction
  • Ly::Int: number of unit cells in the second lattice direction
  • t::Real: nearest-neighbor hopping amplitude (default 1.0; positive convention)

Return

A sorted Vector{Float64} of length LxВ·Ly.

References

G. H. Wannier, Phys. Rev. 79, 357 (1950).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::RFIM, ::CriticalTemperature, ::Infinite; d::Int, J=m.J, О”=m.О”)
    -> Float64

Critical temperature of the RFIM as a function of spatial dimension d. In the Imry-Ma regime d вүӨ 2 at non-zero disorder О” > 0 long-range order is destroyed and T_c = 0.

For d вүҘ 3 (Imbrie 1985 / Bricmont-Kupiainen 1988 rigorous FM phase) T_c(d, J, О”) > 0 but no closed-form analytic value is known and a DomainError is raised вҖ” Phase 2 will plug in numerical-reference values (e.g. Monte-Carlo at d = 3). At О” = 0 the model reduces to the pure Ising model and the call is deferred to that model's CriticalTemperature entry; here we also raise DomainError.

References

  • Y. Imry, S. Ma, Phys. Rev. Lett. 35, 1399 (1975).
  • J. Imbrie, Comm. Math. Phys. 98, 145 (1985).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::RandomBondIsing2D, ::CentralCharge, ::Infinite; p=m.p) -> Rational

Central charge of the 2D ВұJ random-bond Ising model along the phase-diagram slice selected by p.

Phase 1 exposes only the pure ferromagnetic critical line p = 1, where the model is in the 2D Ising universality class (Onsager 1944) with c = 1/2, delegated to MinimalModel(4, 3).

For 0 вүӨ p < 1 the Nishimori-line ferromagnet/paramagnet crossover and the multicritical Nishimori point at p вүҲ 0.1093 (Honecker-Picco-Pujol 2001) have unsettled / logarithmic-CFT universality and are deferred to Phase 2 вҖ” these calls raise DomainError.

References

  • L. Onsager, Phys. Rev. 65, 117 (1944).
  • A. Honecker, M. Picco, P. Pujol, Phys. Rev. Lett. 87, 047201 (2001).

Bulk gap of the spin-1 anisotropic chain at the D = 0 reference point, delegated to S1Heisenberg1D: Haldane gap О” вүҲ 0.41048 J (White-Huse 1993 DMRG, numerical-exact).

D вү  0 raises DomainError вҖ” Phase 2. At finite D the system crosses

  • a Gaussian (c = 1) transition near D вүҲ 0.97 J separating Haldane from the large-D phase (Chen-Roncaglia 2008), and
  • an Ising (c = 1/2) transition near D вүҲ вҲ’0.31 J separating Haldane from the easy-axis NГ©el phase (Tzeng-Yang-Hsu 2017);

neither phase boundary has a closed-form expression in D/J.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::SLEkappa, ::CentralCharge, ::Infinite; Оә=m.Оә) -> Float64

Central charge of the CFT dual to SLE_Оә (Bauer-Bernard 2006):

c(Оә) = (3 Оә вҲ’ 8) (6 вҲ’ Оә) / (2 Оә),    Оә > 0.

The map is symmetric under Оә вҶ” 16/Оә, encoding the SLE duality between a chordal curve and its outer-boundary curve. Canonical fixed points return the expected rational values: c(2) = -2, c(8/3) = 0, c(3) = 1/2, c(4) = 1, c(6) = 0, c(8) = -2.

Оә вүӨ 0 raises DomainError (the SLE process is undefined at and below zero diffusivity).

References

  • M. Bauer, D. Bernard, Phys. Rep. 432, 115 (2006).
  • J. Cardy, Annals Phys. 318, 81 (2005).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::SLEkappa, ::FractalDimension, ::Infinite; Оә=m.Оә) -> Float64

Hausdorff dimension of the SLE_Оә random curve (Beffara 2008):

d_H(Оә) = min(2, 1 + Оә/8),    Оә > 0.

The cap at d_H = 2 for Оә вүҘ 8 reflects the space-filling regime (the SLEОә curve becomes space-filling at Оә = 8 and stays so beyond, so its Hausdorff dimension cannot exceed the ambient plane). Canonical fixed points evaluate to: `dH(2)=5/4,dH(8/3)=4/3,dH(3)=11/8,dH(4)=3/2,dH(6)=7/4,d_H(8)=2`.

Оә вүӨ 0 raises DomainError (the SLE process is undefined at and below zero diffusivity).

References

  • V. Beffara, Annals Probab. 36, 1421 (2008).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::SYK, ::ConformalWeights, ::Infinite;
      q::Integer = m.q, field::Symbol = :ПҲ, kwargs...) -> Rational{Int}

Large-N IR (low-energy / emergent-conformal) Majorana fermion conformal dimension of the Sachdev-Ye-Kitaev model:

О”_ПҲ = 1 / q.

This is the universal scaling of the disorder-averaged two-point function

вҹЁПҲ(П„_1) ПҲ(П„_2)вҹ© вҲқ 1 / |П„_12|^{2 О”_ПҲ}

in the IR conformal window where the Schwarzian reparametrisation soft mode dominates the dynamics (Kitaev 2015; Maldacena-Stanford 2016). Finite-N and subleading-1/(ОІJ) Schwarzian corrections, as well as composite-operator dimensions (the O_n = ПҲ вҲӮ_П„^{2n+1} ПҲ bilinear tower), are deferred to Phase 2.

Arguments

  • q::Integer = m.q: body-count of the Majorana coupling. Must be even and вүҘ 2.
  • field::Symbol = :ПҲ: which IR operator to query. Phase 1 supports only :ПҲ (the elementary Majorana fermion); any other symbol raises DomainError, deferring composite-operator dimensions to Phase 2.

References

  • S. Sachdev, J. Ye, Phys. Rev. Lett. 70, 3339 (1993).
  • A. Kitaev, KITP talks (2015).
  • J. Maldacena, D. Stanford, Phys. Rev. D 94, 106002 (2016).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::SchwingerModel, ::ChiralCondensate, ::Infinite; e=model.e) -> Float64

Anomaly-induced chiral condensate in the massless Schwinger model (Schwinger 1962; Coleman-Jackiw-Susskind 1975):

вҹЁПҲМ„ПҲвҹ© = вҲ’ exp(Оі_E) В· e / (2ПҖ^{3/2}),

where Оі_E вүҲ 0.5772156649 is the Euler-Mascheroni constant. Negative by convention; magnitude scales linearly with the gauge coupling. The non-zero condensate is the canonical 1+1-D example of anomaly- induced spontaneous chiral-symmetry breaking: the classical Lagrangian is chirally symmetric, but the axial U(1) anomaly forces вҹЁПҲМ„ПҲвҹ© вү  0 in the quantum vacuum.

e > 0 required.

References

  • J. Schwinger, Phys. Rev. 128, 2425 (1962).
  • S. Coleman, R. Jackiw, L. Susskind, Annals Phys. 93, 267 (1975).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::SixVertex, ::FreeEnergy, ::Infinite; beta::Real = Inf, kwargs...) -> Float64

Free-energy density per vertex of the six-vertex model in the thermodynamic limit, dispatched on the Lieb phase parameter О” = (aВІ + bВІ вҲ’ cВІ) / (2 a b).

  • Ferroelectric (О” > 1) вҖ” frozen ground state, closed form

    f = вҲ’log max(a, b)             (Lieb 1967c)

    Implemented exactly.

  • Square-ice point (a = b = c) вҖ” Lieb 1967a closed form, f = вҲ’(3/2) log(4/3). Implemented exactly.

  • Generic disordered (|О”| вүӨ 1, off the square-ice diagonal) вҖ” Lieb / Sutherland 1967 trigonometric integral. Deferred in this commit (Phase 2 of issue #163); the precise normalisation across the full disordered region needs the careful Baxter В§8.8 bookkeeping that we have not yet validated robustly. Calls in this region throw an informative ArgumentError.

  • Antiferroelectric (О” < вҲ’1) вҖ” Lieb 1967b elliptic-function form, deferred in this commit (Phase 3 of issue #163). Calls throw an informative ArgumentError.

The beta kwarg is accepted for API symmetry with other classical fetches but does not enter the closed forms: the temperature scale is already absorbed into the weights (a, b, c).

References

  • E. H. Lieb, Phys. Rev. 162, 162 (1967a) вҖ” square ice / disordered.
  • E. H. Lieb, Phys. Rev. Lett. 18, 1046 (1967b) вҖ” antiferroelectric.
  • E. H. Lieb, Phys. Rev. Lett. 19, 108 (1967c) вҖ” KDP / ferroelectric.
  • B. Sutherland, Phys. Rev. Lett. 19, 103 (1967) вҖ” disordered phase trigonometric integral.
  • R. J. Baxter, Exactly Solved Models in Statistical Mechanics (Academic Press, 1982), В§В§8.8вҖ“8.10.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::SixVertex, ::ResidualEntropy, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> Float64

Zero-temperature configurational entropy per vertex of the six-vertex model on the infinite square lattice.

  • Square ice (a = b = c, equivalently О” = 1/2) вҖ” Lieb 1967a closed form

    S/N = (3/2) log(4/3) вүҲ 0.4315231087вҖҰ

  • Ferroelectric phase (О” > 1) вҖ” frozen ground state, a single ordered configuration up to global symmetry, so S_residual = 0.

  • Disordered phase off the square-ice point and antiferroelectric phase (О” < вҲ’1) вҖ” the residual entropy is not yet implemented by this method and the call throws an informative ArgumentError. The disordered-phase formula is the Lieb / Sutherland 1967 trigonometric integral evaluated at zero temperature; the AFE branch is the Lieb 1967b elliptic-function form. Both are tracked as follow-up scope.

  • E. H. Lieb, Phys. Rev. 162, 162 (1967a) вҖ” square ice.
  • E. H. Lieb, Phys. Rev. Lett. 18, 1046 (1967b) вҖ” F-model / AFE.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::SpinIce, ::ResidualEntropy, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> Float64

Zero-temperature residual entropy per spin of pyrochlore spin ice in the Pauling 1935 closed form

S/N = (1/2) log(3/2) вүҲ 0.20273.

The estimate ignores ice-rule correlations between neighbouring tetrahedra; subsequent series (Nagle 1966) and numerical transfer matrix studies put the true value a few percent higher. The textbook closed form is shipped here because it is exact under the mean-tetrahedron approximation and remains the canonical constant-of-Nature for spin-ice phenomenology.

References

  • L. Pauling, J. Am. Chem. Soc. 57, 2680 (1935).
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::Symbol, q::Symbol, bc::BoundaryCondition = Infinite(); kwargs...)

Deprecated in v0.13. Prefer the concrete-struct form:

fetch(TFIM(; J=1.0, h=1.0), Energy(), OBC(N=24); beta=5.0)

This symbol-based signature is kept for drop-in backward compatibility вҖ” the call is routed through Model(m; kwargs...) + Quantity(q) and forwarded to the concrete fetch(::AbstractQAtlasModel, ::AbstractQuantity, ::BoundaryCondition) method registered by each model. A one-shot informational log is emitted the first time the shim is reached from a given site.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::TASEP, ::SteadyStateCurrent, ::Infinite; p=m.p, ПҒ=m.ПҒ) -> Float64

Mean-field steady-state particle current of TASEP at hopping rate p > 0 and density 0 вүӨ ПҒ вүӨ 1 (Derrida-Lebowitz 1998):

j(ПҒ) = p ПҒ (1 вҲ’ ПҒ).

Special points:

  • ПҒ = 1/2 вҶ’ j_max = p/4 (maximal current, half-filling)
  • ПҒ = 0 or ПҒ = 1 вҶ’ j = 0 (empty / fully packed lattice)
  • ПҒ вҶ” 1 вҲ’ ПҒ (particle-hole symmetry)

p вүӨ 0 or ПҒ вҲү [0, 1] raises DomainError.

References

  • B. Derrida, J. L. Lebowitz, Phys. Rev. Lett. 80, 209 (1998).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::CentralCharge, ::Infinite) -> Float64

Central charge of the TFIM:

  • c = 1/2 at the critical point h = J (Ising CFT)
  • c = 0 in either gapped phase (h вү  J) вҖ” no low-energy CFT description

Criticality is detected by |h/J - 1| вүӨ 1e-6.

Example

julia> QAtlas.fetch(TFIM(), CentralCharge(), Infinite())
0.5

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::CorrelationLength, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> Float64

T = 0 longitudinal correlation length of the infinite TFIM,

Оҫ = 1 / (2|h - J|)        (gapped phase)
Оҫ = Inf                   (critical point h = J)

This is set by the inverse mass gap О” = 2|h - J| (see MassGap at Infinite); the asymptotic exponential decay of the connected longitudinal correlator is e^{-r/Оҫ}.

In QAtlas convention Оҫ is dimensionless (in units of the lattice spacing).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::TFIM, ::CriticalExponents, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> NamedTuple

Onsager 2D-Ising critical exponents at the TFIM quantum critical point h = J, delegated to the existing Universality(:Ising) infrastructure at d = 2:

ОІ = 1/8,  Оі = 7/4,  Оҙ = 15,  ОҪ = 1,  Оұ = 0,  О· = 1/4.

The 1D TFIM is exactly equivalent to the 2D classical Ising model via the quantum-classical mapping (Pfeuty 1970), so the universal critical exponents are identical to Onsager's 1944 result.

References

  • L. Onsager, Phys. Rev. 65, 117 (1944) вҖ” 2D classical Ising exact solution.
  • P. Pfeuty, Ann. Phys. 57, 79 (1970) вҖ” TFIM вҶ” 2D Ising equivalence.
  • S. Sachdev, Quantum Phase Transitions (2nd ed., Cambridge 2011) вҖ” TFIM as canonical QPT example.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::EnergyLocal, bc::OBC; beta::Float64, kwargs...)
    -> Vector{Float64}

Site-local energy density Оө_i of the OBC TFIM at inverse temperature beta, defined so that ОЈбөў Оө_i = вҹЁHвҹ©_ОІ. Each bond is split symmetrically between its two endpoints:

Оө_i = -(J/2) (вҹЁПғб¶»_{i-1} Пғб¶»_iвҹ©_ОІ + вҹЁПғб¶»_i Пғб¶»_{i+1}вҹ©_ОІ) - h вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©_ОІ

with the missing bonds at the i = 1 and i = N boundaries taken to be zero. Bond expectations are read off as ОЈ(ОІ)[2i, 2i+1] from the Majorana thermal covariance (exact, O(N) after the single 2NГ—2N diagonalisation).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::Energy{:per_site}, ::Infinite; beta, betas) -> Float64 or Vector{Float64}

Energy per site вҹЁHвҹ©/N in the thermodynamic limit (PBC, N вҶ’ вҲһ). Native granularity at Infinite() (total energy diverges and has no defined value here).

Оө(ОІ) = -(1/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk  Оӣ(k)/2 В· tanh(ОІ Оӣ(k) / 2)

where the PBC dispersion is Оӣ(k) = 2вҲҡ(JВІ + hВІ - 2Jh cos k).

  • beta::Float64: return scalar Оө(ОІ)
  • betas::AbstractVector{Float64}: return vector
  • no keyword: return ground-state energy per site (ОІ вҶ’ вҲһ)

Uses adaptive Gauss-Kronrod quadrature (QuadGK).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::Energy{:total}, bc::OBC; beta, betas) -> Float64 or Vector{Float64}

Total energy вҹЁHвҹ©(ОІ) for the OBC TFIM with N sites. Native granularity for finite-N TFIM (per-site is provided by the generic conversion fallback in src/core/quantities.jl).

  • N is read from bc.N (OBC(N) / OBC(; N)) or from kwargs[:N] as a legacy fallback.

  • betas::AbstractVector{Float64}: return vector, reusing spectrum (O(NВі) once)

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::FidelitySusceptibility, ::Infinite;
      rtol::Float64=1e-10, kwargs...) -> Float64

Per-site fidelity susceptibility ПҮ_F / L of the infinite TFIM with respect to the transverse field h, computed by GaussвҖ“Kronrod quadrature of the closed-form Bogoliubov-vacuum overlap integral.

Closed-form values (h вү  J):

ПҮ_F / L = 1 / (16 (JВІ вҲ’ hВІ))            (ordered, h < J)
ПҮ_F / L = JВІ / (16 hВІ (hВІ вҲ’ JВІ))         (disordered, h > J)

Both branches diverge as 1 / |J вҲ’ h| at the critical point |h| = J вҖ” a DomainError is thrown if ||h| вҲ’ |J|| is below 1e-14.

References: Gu, Int. J. Mod. Phys. B 24, 4371 (2010); Damski, PRB 87, 165101 (2013).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::FidelitySusceptibility, bc::OBC;
      per_site::Bool=false, kwargs...) -> Float64

Ground-state fidelity susceptibility ПҮ_F of the OBC TFIM with N = bc.N sites with respect to the transverse field h:

ПҮ_F(h) = ОЈ_{n вү  0} |вҹЁn | вҲӮ_h H | 0вҹ©|ВІ / (E_n - E_0)ВІ,

evaluated in closed form via the Bogoliubov diagonalisation (no numerical differentiation). Cost O(NВі).

per_site=true returns ПҮ_F / N.

References: Gu, Int. J. Mod. Phys. B 24, 4371 (2010); Damski, PRB 87, 165101 (2013).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model_f::TFIM, ::GGEValue{Energy{:per_site}}, ::Infinite;
      initial::TFIM, kwargs...) -> Float64

Per-site Generalised Gibbs Ensemble (GGE) energy density of the infinite TFIM after a sudden quench (J, h_0) вҶ’ (J, h_f), with model_f = TFIM(J = J, h = h_f) and initial = TFIM(J = J, h = h_0).

The closed form

Оө_GGE = -(1/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk В· (Оӣ_k(h_f)/2) В· (1 вҲ’ 2 n_k(h_0, h_f))

is the long-time average reached by the post-quench evolution; it also equals the (time-independent) energy expectation of the initial state |ПҲ0вҹ© in the post-quench Hamiltonian Hf, which serves as the canonical energy-conservation cross-check.

Required kwarg

  • initial::TFIM вҖ” pre-quench TFIM whose ground state is the initial state. The Ising couplings must match (initial.J == model_f.J); a mismatch throws DomainError.

Example

fetch(TFIM(J = 1.0, h = 0.5), GGEValue(Energy(:per_site)), Infinite();
      initial = TFIM(J = 1.0, h = 2.0))

References

  • Rigol et al., Relaxation in a Completely Integrable Many-Body Quantum System, PRL 98, 050405 (2007).
  • Calabrese, Essler, Fagotti, Quantum Quench in the Transverse Field Ising Chain, J. Stat. Mech. (2012) P07016, P07022.
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model_f::TFIM, ::GGEValue{MagnetizationX}, ::Infinite;
      initial::TFIM, kwargs...) -> Float64

GGE stationary value of the transverse magnetisation вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ© of the infinite TFIM after a sudden quench (J, h_0) вҶ’ (J, h_f):

вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©_GGE = (2/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk В· (h_f вҲ’ J cos k)/Оӣ_k(h_f) В· (1 вҲ’ 2 n_k)

with n_k = sinВІ(Оё_k(h_0) вҲ’ Оё_k(h_f)).

Required kwarg

  • initial::TFIM вҖ” pre-quench TFIM (must share J).

References

See [fetch(::TFIM, ::GGEValue{Energy{:per_site}}, ::Infinite; ...)].

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model_f::TFIM, ::LoschmidtEcho{:amplitude}, bc::OBC;
      initial::TFIM, t::Real, kwargs...) -> Float64

Loschmidt echo L(t) = |вҹЁПҲ_0|e^{-iH_f t}|ПҲ_0вҹ©|ВІ for an OBC chain of size bc.N after a sudden quench H_0 = TFIM(J, h_0) вҶ’ H_f = TFIM(J, h_f).

initial carries the pre-quench Hamiltonian (must share J with model_f; only h differs). Computed by diagonalising both BdG matrices and evaluating the per-mode Bogoliubov overlap product.

References: Heyl-Polkovnikov-Kehrein, PRL 110, 135704 (2013); Heyl, Rep. Prog. Phys. 81, 054001 (2018).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method

      initial::TFIM, t::Real, atol::Real=1e-10, rtol::Real=1e-8, kwargs...)
    -> Float64

Loschmidt rate function in the thermodynamic limit:

О»(t) = -(1/2ПҖ) вҲ«_0^ПҖ log| cosВІ(О”Оё_k) + sinВІ(О”Оё_k) e^{-2 i Оӣ_k^{(f)} t} |ВІ dk,

evaluated by QuadGK.quadgk. At a DQPT critical time the integrand has a log-divergence at k = k^*; QuadGK's adaptive subdivision handles the integrable singularity.

References: Heyl-Polkovnikov-Kehrein, PRL 110, 135704 (2013); Heyl, Rep. Prog. Phys. 81, 054001 (2018).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model_f::TFIM, ::MagnetizationXLocal{:quench}, ::Infinite;
      initial::TFIM, t::Real, kwargs...) -> Float64

Translationally-invariant вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©(t) for the infinite TFIM after a sudden quench from H(initial.h) to H(model_f.h) (initial.J == model_f.J required). Closed-form k-integral:

вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©(t) = (1/ПҖ) вҲ«вӮҖ^ПҖ dk [ cos(2 Оё_k^f) cos(2 О”Оё_k)
                        + sin(2 Оё_k^f) sin(2 О”Оё_k) cos(2 Оӣ_k^f t) ]

with О”Оёk вүЎ Оёk(hf) вҲ’ Оёk(h_0), evaluated by adaptive GaussвҖ“Kronrod quadrature.

References: BarouchвҖ“McCoyвҖ“Dresden, PRA 2 (1970); CalabreseвҖ“EsslerвҖ“ Fagotti, J. Stat. Mech. P07016 (2012).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model_f::TFIM, ::MagnetizationXLocal{:quench}, bc::OBC;
      initial::TFIM, i::Int, t::Real, kwargs...) -> Float64

Time-evolved local transverse magnetisation вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©(t) of the OBC TFIM after a sudden quench.

  • model_f is the post-quench model (sets h_f, J).
  • initial is the pre-quench TFIM whose ground state |ПҲ_0вҹ© is the initial state. Both models must share the same J; mismatch raises an ArgumentError (the quench is not defined for a J вҶ’ J' jump in the current implementation).
  • i вҲҲ 1:N, t вҲҲ в„қ, N from bc.N (or kwargs).

Implementation: Majorana covariance evolution ОЈ(t) = R(t) ОЈ0 R(t)^T with ОЈ0 = GS covariance under H(h0) and R(t) = exp(hf В· t). Cost per call: one 2N Г— 2N eigendecomposition + one matrix exponential.

Sanity checks (covered by test/standalone/test_tfim_sigma_x_quench.jl):

  • t = 0 вҶ’ equilibrium вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ© of GS(h_0).
  • h0 = hf вҶ’ time-independent (= equilibrium GS at h_0).
  • Large-N central-site вҶ’ matches the Infinite() closed form.

References: BarouchвҖ“McCoyвҖ“Dresden, Phys. Rev. A 2 (1970) 1075; CalabreseвҖ“EsslerвҖ“Fagotti, J. Stat. Mech. P07016 (2012).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::MagnetizationY, bc::OBC; beta) -> Float64

Per-site bulk magnetisation вҹЁОЈбөў ПғКёбөўвҹ©_ОІ / N of the OBC TFIM. Identically zero in any Gaussian state because ПғКё_i reduces to an odd product of Majoranas. Returned as exact 0.0 so callers can use it as a deterministic baseline against random-sample estimators that fluctuate around zero.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::MagnetizationZ, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> Float64

Spontaneous longitudinal magnetisation per site of the infinite TFIM at T = 0, m_z = (1 - (h/J)ВІ)^{1/8} for h < J, else 0 (Pfeuty 1970). Returns the positive branch of the ZвӮӮ-broken doublet.

The result is the T = 0 order parameter; the function does not take a beta kwarg because m_z(T > 0) = 0 for any finite chain in the thermodynamic limit (Mermin-Wagner is irrelevant in 1D, but the broken phase requires explicit symmetry breaking; m_z(T,h) вү  0 only at T = 0). Pass beta = Inf if you want to be explicit; it is ignored.

source

Identically zero in the OBC TFIM by the ZвӮӮ symmetry Пғб¶» вҶ’ вҲ’Пғб¶» of the Hamiltonian (Gaussian state, odd product of Majoranas). Returned as an explicit zero vector so consumers can use it as an exact baseline against finite random-sample estimates that fluctuate around zero.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::MassGap, ::Infinite) -> Float64

Mass gap of the infinite-chain TFIM: the lowest single-quasiparticle excitation energy

О” = min_k Оӣ(k),     Оӣ(k) = 2 вҲҡ( JВІ + hВІ вҲ’ 2 J h cos k ).

Closed form:

О” = 2 |h вҲ’ J|.

Canonical values:

  • ordered (h < J): О” = 2(J вҲ’ h)
  • disordered (h > J): О” = 2(h вҲ’ J)
  • critical (h = J): О” = 0 (Ising CFT, О” ~ ПҖ v_F / N on finite chains)
source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::MassGap, bc::OBC) -> Float64

Single-quasiparticle gap of the N-site OBC TFIM read off the BdG spectrum as Оӣ_min, the smallest positive eigenvalue of the 2NГ—2N Bogoliubov-de Gennes Hamiltonian.

This is the one-particle excitation energy. Away from the critical point (|h вҲ’ J| > O(1/N)) it converges to 2|h вҲ’ J| exponentially in N. At the critical point h = J the OBC gap scales as О”(N) ~ ПҖ J / N (Ising CFT).

Size is taken from bc.N (or kwargs[:N] as a legacy fallback).

source

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, q::RenyiEntropy, ::Infinite;
      в„“::Int, beta::Real = Inf, kwargs...) -> Float64

Calabrese-Cardy RГ©nyi-Оұ entanglement entropy of a contiguous block of length в„“ in the infinite TFIM. Coefficient

P_Оұ = (c / 6) В· (1 + 1/Оұ),  c = 1/2.
  • T = 0, critical: S_Оұ = P_Оұ В· log(2 в„“)
  • T = 0, gapped : S_Оұ = (P_Оұ / 2) В· log(2 Оҫ sinh(в„“/Оҫ)), Оҫ = 1/(2|h - J|)
  • T > 0, critical: S_Оұ = P_Оұ В· log[(2 ОІ/ПҖ) sinh(ПҖ в„“ / ОІ)]
  • T > 0, gapped : not implemented (errors out).

The non-universal S_0 offset is dropped.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, q::RenyiEntropy, bc::OBC;
      в„“::Int, beta::Float64 = Inf, kwargs...) -> Float64

RГ©nyi entropy of order Оұ = q.Оұ (Оұ вү  1) for the first в„“ spins of the N-site OBC TFIM in the thermal state at inverse temperature beta (or the ground state when beta = Inf), via Peschel's correlation-matrix method вҖ” see equation (2) in the file header.

The Gaussian factorisation gives S_Оұ = ОЈ_k s_Оұ(ОҪ_k), where the ОҪk are the non-negative eigenvalues of `i ОЈA`. As for the von Neumann case, the JW-factorisation argument (FagottiвҖ“Calabrese 2010) means the fermion RГ©nyi entropy equals the spin RГ©nyi entropy for a contiguous block.

Оұ = 1 is rejected at the RenyiEntropy constructor; use VonNeumannEntropy explicitly.

Cost is O(в„“Ві) from the Hermitian eigendecomposition of i ОЈ_A, identical to the von Neumann path.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::SusceptibilityYY, bc::OBC; beta) -> Float64

Per-site equal-time fluctuation ПҮ_yy(ОІ) = (ОІ / N) В· ОЈ_{i,j} вҹЁПғКё_i ПғКё_jвҹ©_ОІ of the OBC TFIM. вҹЁПғКёвҹ© = 0 in this Gaussian state, so the variance form simplifies to (ОІ/N) В· вҹЁM_yВІвҹ©.

Implementation: per pair (i, j) evaluate the Pfaffian of the static Majorana Wick matrix. Diagonal contribution вҹЁ(ПғКёбөў)ВІвҹ© = 1 (Pauli identity) is added directly, off-diagonal twice (symmetric). Cost is O(NВІ В· MВі) with M = 2 max(i, j) вҲ’ 1; same scaling as SusceptibilityXX OBC and _xx_uniform_susceptibility in TFIM_thermal.jl.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::SusceptibilityZZ, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, Пү::Union{Real,Nothing} = nothing,
      q::Union{Real,Nothing} = nothing,
      N_proxy::Int = 64, t_max::Real = 20.0, dt::Real = 0.1, kwargs...)
    -> Float64

Longitudinal susceptibility of the infinite TFIM. This router dispatches on Пү:

  • Пү === nothing (default) вҶ’ static uniform isothermal susceptibility ПҮ_zz(ОІ) at q = 0, the same large-N OBC proxy _zz_uniform_susceptibility previously exposed in TFIM_zaxis.jl (default N_proxy = 80). q is ignored on this branch.

  • Пү::Real вҶ’ dynamic imaginary part ПҮ''_zz(q, Пү; ОІ) at finite momentum, computed via the Kubo commutator formula

    ПҮ''_zz(q, Пү; ОІ) = (1/2) вҲ«dt e^{iПүt} В· (1/N_b) ОЈ_{i,j вҲҲ bulk}
                        e^{-iq(i-j)} вҹЁ[Пғб¶»_i(t), Пғб¶»_j(0)]вҹ©_ОІ

    (Kubo 1957; Mahan, Many-Particle Physics, ch. 3) on the same N_proxy-site OBC chain as ZZStructureFactor's dynamic branch. q is required on this branch; ArgumentError is raised if absent.

    Default N_proxy = 64, t_max = 20.0, dt = 0.1 mirror the dynamic ZZStructureFactor proxy so the two are directly comparable (e.g. for fluctuationвҖ“dissipation cross-checks); the same Пү-resolution ~ ПҖ/t_max, UV cutoff ~ ПҖ/dt, and finite-bulk exponential corrections apply.

The static and dynamic branches answer different physical questions: the static path returns the equilibrium thermodynamic susceptibility (integral of ПҮ''(Пү)/Пү weighted by tanh(ОІПү/2)), while the dynamic path returns the spectral function at a single (q, Пү). The static branch is the recommended one for sum-rule / equation-of-state work.

FDT cross-check is not an independent physics anchor

The dynamic ПҮ'' branch shares the OBC large-N Pfaffian / Majorana machinery (and (N_proxy, t_max, dt) discretisation) with the ZZStructureFactor dynamic branch. Asserting S = 2ПҮ''/(1вҲ’e^{-ОІПү}) therefore primarily verifies the commutator-vs-product structure is consistent вҖ” both spectral functions are computed from the same cached ОЈ_thermal and R(t) = exp(h_majorana В· t), so their discretisation errors are correlated. Stronger independent anchors are: (i) the f-sum rule вҲ«вӮҖ^вҲһ Пү ПҮ''(q,Пү) dПү relates analytically to ВҪвҹЁ[[H, Пғб¶»q], Пғб¶»{-q}]вҹ© (Hohenberg-Brinkman 1974); and (ii) at h = 0 the Пғб¶» operator commutes with H, so ПҮ''_zz(q,Пү) вүЎ 0 вҖ” a trivial-but-strong test that fails fast on any sign error.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::VonNeumannEntropy{:equilibrium}, ::Infinite;
      в„“::Int, beta::Real = Inf, kwargs...) -> Float64

Calabrese-Cardy von Neumann entanglement entropy of a contiguous block of length в„“ in the infinite TFIM (Ising CFT, c = 1/2). Returns the universal leading-log term; the non-universal S_0 offset is dropped.

  • beta = Inf (default): T = 0 ground state.
  • beta < вҲһ : finite-temperature thermal state.

At criticality (h вүҲ J) and T = 0 the result is (c/3) log(2 в„“). In a gapped phase at T = 0 the result is (c/6) log(2 Оҫ sinh(в„“/Оҫ)) with Оҫ = 1/(2|h - J|); this saturates at (c/6)(в„“/Оҫ + log Оҫ + log 2) for в„“ вү« Оҫ (area law set by Оҫ). At criticality + finite T the result is (c/3) log[(2 ОІ/ПҖ) sinh(ПҖ в„“ / ОІ)], consistent with the T = 0 form under ОІ вҶ’ вҲһ. The off-critical + finite-T case errors out (not yet implemented).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::VonNeumannEntropy{:equilibrium}, bc::OBC;
      в„“::Int, beta::Float64 = Inf, kwargs...) -> Float64

Von Neumann entanglement entropy of the first в„“ spins of the N-site OBC TFIM in the thermal state at inverse temperature beta (or the ground state when beta = Inf), computed by Peschel's correlation- matrix method вҖ” see equation (1) in the file header.

  • N = _bc_size(bc, kwargs) (read from OBC(N) or legacy kwargs[:N]).
  • в„“ must satisfy 1 вүӨ в„“ вүӨ N - 1.
  • Cost is O(в„“Ві); for typical N = 200, в„“ = 100 this runs in a few milliseconds, whereas the full-ED SVD baseline scales as O(4^N).

The result matches the full-ED reference at every small N (verified to 1e-10 in test/models/test_TFIM_entanglement.jl).

See full derivation in docs/src/calc/jw-tfim-bdg.md.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model_f::TFIM, ::VonNeumannEntropy{:quench}, bc::OBC;
      initial::TFIM, в„“::Int, t::Real, kwargs...) -> Float64

Post-quench von Neumann entanglement entropy of the first в„“ sites of the N-site OBC TFIM.

Prepare the chain in the ground state of initial::TFIM and quench instantly to model_f::TFIM; this method returns

S(в„“, t) = -Tr ПҒ_A(t) log ПҒ_A(t)

evaluated by Peschel's correlation-matrix method on the time-evolved Majorana covariance ОЈ(t) = R(t) ОЈ0 R(t)бөҖ. See the file header (`TFIMquench_entanglement.jl`) for the full derivation and the CalabreseвҖ“Cardy quasi-particle picture for the expected linear-growth behaviour.

Required keyword arguments

  • initial::TFIM вҖ” initial-Hamiltonian model whose ground state is the t = 0 state.
  • в„“::Int вҖ” subsystem length, 1 вүӨ в„“ вүӨ N - 1.
  • t::Real вҖ” post-quench time.

N is read from OBC(N) (or legacy kwargs[:N]). At t = 0 the result coincides with the equilibrium VonNeumannEntropy{:equilibrium} of the initial model вҖ” this is the back-compat sanity check exercised in test/standalone/test_tfim_quench_entanglement.jl.

Cost: O(NВі) from the matrix exponential plus O(в„“Ві) from the Peschel eigendecomposition.

References: CalabreseвҖ“Cardy J. Stat. Mech. P04010 (2005); Peschel J. Phys. A 36, L205 (2003).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::XXCorrelation{:connected}, bc::OBC;
      beta::Real = Inf, i::Int, j::Int, kwargs...) -> Float64

Connected static thermal transverse correlator вҹЁПғЛЈ_i ПғЛЈ_jвҹ©_ОІ вҲ’ вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©_ОІ вҹЁПғЛЈ_jвҹ©_ОІ for the OBC TFIM.

Unlike ZZCorrelation{:connected} (where вҹЁПғб¶»вҹ© = 0 by ZвӮӮ on OBC and the connected and bare correlators coincide), вҹЁПғЛЈвҹ©_ОІ вү  0 in general вҖ” ПғЛЈ is the field-coupled order parameter and acquires a non-zero expectation ОЈ[2i-1, 2i] from the BdG-thermal covariance.

For i = j the on-site ПғЛЈ variance simplifies to 1 вҲ’ вҹЁПғЛЈ_iвҹ©ВІ since (ПғЛЈ)ВІ = I.

Internals: a single 2N Г— 2N BdG diagonalisation gives both the ПғЛЈ expectation values (read off the covariance ОЈ) and, with the identity evolution R = I at t = 0, the 4Г—4 Pfaffian for вҹЁПғЛЈ_i ПғЛЈ_jвҹ©_ОІ.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::XXCorrelation{:static}, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real = Inf, i::Int, j::Int,
      N_proxy::Int = 80, kwargs...) -> Float64

Static вҹЁПғЛЈ_i ПғЛЈ_jвҹ©_ОІ in the thermodynamic limit, delivered as the OBC value at proxy size N_proxy (default 80) вҖ” same compromise as SusceptibilityZZ/ZZStructureFactor at Infinite(), see TFIM_zaxis.jl for the rationale.

The caller is responsible for picking bulk-friendly indices, e.g. N_proxy / 4 вүӨ i, j вүӨ 3 N_proxy / 4. At those interior sites the boundary contamination decays exponentially with the distance to the nearest edge in the gapped phase, and as 1/distance at criticality.

Raise N_proxy if more accuracy is needed; the cost is the single 2 N_proxy Г— 2 N_proxy BdG diagonalisation.

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::XXCorrelation{:static}, bc::OBC;
      beta::Real = Inf, i::Int, j::Int, kwargs...) -> Float64

Static (equal-time) thermal transverse correlator вҹЁПғЛЈ_i ПғЛЈ_jвҹ©_ОІ for the OBC TFIM at inverse temperature beta. beta = Inf (the default) gives the ground-state value.

Implementation: re-uses _sx_sx_corr(N, J, h, i, j, 0.0; ОІ=beta) from TFIM_dynamics.jl вҖ” a 4Г—4 Pfaffian over the four Majoranas (Оі_{2i-1}, Оі_{2i}, Оі_{2j-1}, Оі_{2j}). The result is real at equal time, so the imaginary residue (round-off) is dropped via real(...).

At i = j, вҹЁ(ПғЛЈ)ВІвҹ© = вҹЁIвҹ© = 1 regardless of (ОІ, J, h).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::ZZCorrelation{:connected}, bc::OBC;
      beta::Float64, [i::Int, j::Int]) -> Matrix{Float64} or Float64

Connected static thermal correlator C^c_{ij} = вҹЁПғб¶»_i Пғб¶»_jвҹ©_ОІ вҲ’ вҹЁПғб¶»_iвҹ©_ОІ вҹЁПғб¶»_jвҹ©_ОІ for the OBC TFIM.

In the OBC TFIM the ZвӮӮ symmetry Пғб¶» вҶ’ вҲ’Пғб¶» is unbroken at any finite N (Gaussian state of the JW fermions; odd-product expectation vanishes), so вҹЁПғб¶»_iвҹ©_ОІ = 0 and the connected correlator coincides with the bare static one. This method therefore re-uses the :static routine and is provided as a separate dispatch for caller clarity / API completeness.

If at some point a TFIM variant breaks ZвӮӮ explicitly (e.g. by adding a longitudinal field), the implementation will still be correct provided the per-site вҹЁПғб¶»_iвҹ©_ОІ is taken from MagnetizationZLocal and subtracted off вҖ” see the comment in the source.

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(model::TFIM, ::ZZStructureFactor, ::Infinite;
      beta::Real, q::Real, Пү::Union{Real,Nothing} = nothing,
      N_proxy::Int = 64, t_max::Real = 20.0, dt::Real = 0.1, kwargs...)
    -> Float64

Longitudinal structure factor S_zz(q, [Пү,] ОІ) of the infinite TFIM. This router dispatches on Пү:

  • Пү === nothing (default) вҶ’ static S_zz(q, ОІ), computed by the large-N OBC proxy _zz_static_structure_factor (default N_proxy = 80; same path as defined in TFIM_zaxis.jl).

  • Пү::Real вҶ’ dynamic S_zz(q, Пү; ОІ), computed as the OBC large-N proxy of the time- and space-Fourier transform of вҹЁПғб¶»_i(t) Пғб¶»_j(0)вҹ©_ОІ,

    S_zz(q, Пү; ОІ) = вҲ«dt e^{iПүt} В· (1/N_b) ОЈ_{i,j вҲҲ bulk}
                      e^{-iq(i-j)} вҹЁПғб¶»_i(t) Пғб¶»_j(0)вҹ©_ОІ,

    with t вҲҲ [-t_max, t_max] discretised at spacing dt and (i, j) restricted to the central bulk window [N/4, 3N/4] of an N_proxy-site OBC chain.

    Default N_proxy = 64, t_max = 20.0, dt = 0.1 is a balance of precision and cost; the dominant errors are (a) Пү-resolution ~ ПҖ/t_max вүҲ 0.157, (b) UV cutoff ~ ПҖ/dt вүҲ 31.4, (c) finite-size finite-bulk corrections ~ exp(вҲ’(N_proxy вҲ’ 4 Оҫ)/Оҫ). Raise the appropriate parameter to tighten any of these.

Performance: O(|ts| В· N_bВІ В· MВі) Pfaffians per (q, Пү) point, where M вүҲ 2 (i + j) вҲ’ 2. At default settings this is ~1 sec/point on a single core after the Majorana eigendecomposition is amortised. Multiple (q, Пү) points should be batched by writing a custom loop that reuses ОЈ and the per-t evolution matrices R(t).

Static path remains the recommended one for any equilibrium sum-rule work; the dynamic path is intended primarily as a benchmark for TPQMPS / DMRG dynamic structure factor reference values.

Per-site grand-potential density of the spinless-fermion t-V chain at inverse temperature ОІ > 0, currently implemented only at V = 0:

Пү(ОІ; t, Ој) = -(1/(ПҖОІ)) вҲ«_0^ПҖ log(1 + e^{-ОІ Оө(k)}) dk,
Оө(k) = -2t cos k - Ој.

V вү  0 raises DomainError (Phase 2 via JW вҶ” XXZ1D).

source
QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(m::TightBindingV1D, ::MassGap, ::Infinite;
      t=m.t, V=m.V, Ој=m.Ој, kwargs...) -> Float64

Single-particle gap of the tight-binding t-V chain at V = 0:

О” = max(0, |Ој| - 2t) .

Gapless inside the band (|Ој| < 2t), zero at the band edges (|Ој| = 2t), linear-in-|Ој| insulator gap outside (|Ој| > 2t).

V вү  0 raises DomainError (Phase 2 via JW вҶ” XXZ1D).

QAtlas.fetch вҖ” Method
fetch(::TodaLattice, ::MassGap, ::Infinite; kwargs...) -> Float64

Small-amplitude phonon gap of the classical Toda lattice around the uniform-spacing ground state. The harmonic expansion gives Пү(k) = 2 вҲҡ(a b) |sin(k/2)|, an acoustic branch vanishing linearly at k = 0. The corresponding mass gap is identically zero for any (a, b) > 0.

References

  • M. Toda, J. Phys. Soc. Jpn. 22, 431 (1967).
  • H. Flaschka, Phys. Rev. B 9, 1924 (1974).
